The [Syrian Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_Air_Force "Syrian Air Force") had fifty planes, the ten newest of which were World War II–generation models.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

France suspended arms sales to Syria, notwithstanding already-signed contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-Zamir2010p22_114-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Zamir2010p22-114">[110]</a></sup>

Lebanon's army was the smallest of the Arab states, consisting of 3,500 soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p27_128-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p27-128">[124]</a></sup> According to Gelber, in June 1947, Ben-Gurion "arrived at an agreement with the Maronite religious leadership in Lebanon that cost a few thousand pounds and kept Lebanon's army out of the War of Independence and the military Arab coalition".<sup id="cite_ref-137"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-137">[133]</a></sup> A token force of 436 soldiers crossed into northern Galilee, seized two villages after a small skirmish, and withdrew.<sup id="cite_ref-Hughes_15-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Hughes-15">[12]</a></sup> Israel then invaded and occupied southern Lebanon until the end of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-138"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-138">[134]</a></sup>

By the time of the second truce, the Egyptians had 20,000 men in the field in thirteen battalions equipped with 135 tanks and 90 [artillery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artillery "Artillery") pieces.<sup id="cite_ref-139"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-139">[135]</a></sup>

During the first truce, the Iraqis increased their force to about 10,000.<sup id="cite_ref-140"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-140">[136]</a></sup> Ultimately, the Iraqi expeditionary force numbered around 18,000 men.<sup id="cite_ref-Tripp2002p73_141-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Tripp2002p73-141">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-142">[138]</a></sup>

Saudi Arabia sent hundreds of volunteers to join the Arab forces. In February 1948, around 800 tribesmen had gathered near [Aqaba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aqaba "Aqaba") to invade the [Negev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev "Negev"), but crossed to Egypt after Saudi rival King Abdallah denied them permission to pass through Jordanian territory.<sup id="cite_ref-143"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-143">[139]</a></sup> The Saudi troops were attached to the Egyptian command throughout the war,<sup id="cite_ref-144"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-144">[140]</a></sup> and estimates of their total strength ranged up to 1,200.<sup id="cite_ref-145"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-145">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-146">[142]</a></sup> By July 1948, the Saudis comprised three brigades within the Egyptian expeditionary force, and were stationed as guards between Gaza city and Rafah.<sup id="cite_ref-147"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-147">[143]</a></sup> This area came under heavy aerial bombardment during [Operation Yoav](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Yoav "Operation Yoav") in October,<sup id="cite_ref-148"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-148">[144]</a></sup> and faced a [land assault](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Horev "Operation Horev") beginning in late December which culminated in the [Battle of Rafah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Rafah_(1949) "Battle of Rafah (1949)") in early January of the new year. With the subsequent armistice of [24 February 1949](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements#With_Egypt "1949 Armistice Agreements") and evacuation of almost 4,000 Arab soldiers and civilians from Gaza, the Saudi contingent withdrew through [Arish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arish "Arish") and returned to Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-149"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-149">[145]</a></sup>

During the first truce, Sudan sent six companies of regular troops to fight alongside the Egyptians.<sup id="cite_ref-150"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-150">[146]</a></sup> Yemen also committed a small expeditionary force to the war effort, and contingents from Morocco joined the Arab armies as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris,_2008,_p._205_7-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris,_2008,_p._205-7">[6]</a></sup>

## Course of the war

At the last moment, several Arab leaders, to avert catastrophe – secretly appealed to the British to hold on in Palestine for at least another year.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p185_151-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p185-151">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tucker528_152-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Tucker528-152">[148]</a></sup>

### First phase: 15 May – 11 June 1948

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/1948_Arab_Israeli_War_-_May_15-June_10.svg/250px-1948_Arab_Israeli_War_-_May_15-June_10.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1948_Arab_Israeli_War_-_May_15-June_10.svg)

Arab offensive, 15 May – 10 June 1948

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Butterfly_Armored-car_Gvar-Am-israel1948.jpg/220px-Butterfly_Armored-car_Gvar-Am-israel1948.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Butterfly_Armored-car_Gvar-Am-israel1948.jpg)

A "Butterfly" improvised armoured car of the Haganah at [Kibbutz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kibbutz "Kibbutz") [Dorot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dorot "Dorot") in the [Negev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev "Negev"), [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel") 1948. The armoured car is based on [CMP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canadian_Military_Pattern_truck "Canadian Military Pattern truck")\-15 truck. The car has brought supply to the kibbutz. The Negev Kibbutz's<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (January 2016)">dubious</span></a> <span>– <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#Bad_English._ALL_kibbutz_children_from_the_Negev_were_evacuated,_or_just_those_from_Dorot?" title="Talk:1948 Arab–Israeli War">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> children were later evacuated by those cars from their kibbutz, before an expected Egyptian Army attack.

The [civil war in Mandatory Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947%E2%80%931948_civil_war_in_Mandatory_Palestine "1947–1948 civil war in Mandatory Palestine") became a war between separate [states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation_state "Nation state") with the [declaration of the establishment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Declaration_of_Independence "Israeli Declaration of Independence") of the [State of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel") on 14 May 1948, a few hours before the termination of the [British Mandate of Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine "Mandatory Palestine") at midnight. The following morning, the [regular armies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regular_army "Regular army") of neighbouring Arab states – [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Egypt "Kingdom of Egypt"), [Transjordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan "Emirate of Transjordan") and [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_Republic_(1946%E2%80%9363) "Syrian Republic (1946–63)") – invaded territories of the former Palestinian mandate allocated for a future Arab state according to the [United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine "United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine").<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA2_153-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-ReferenceA2-153">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-154">[150]</a></sup>

Through [Plan Dalet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plan_Dalet "Plan Dalet"), Zionist forces had already, from 1 April down to 14 May, conducted 8 of its 13 full-scale military operations outside of the area allotted to a Jewish state by partition, and the operational commander [Yigal Allon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yigal_Allon "Yigal Allon") later stated that had it not been for the Arab invasion, Haganah's forces would have reached 'the natural borders of western Israel.'<sup id="cite_ref-155"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-155">[151]</a></sup> Although the Arab invasion was denounced by the United States, the Soviet Union, and UN secretary-general [Trygve Lie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trygve_Lie "Trygve Lie"), it found support from the [Republic of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949) "Republic of China (1912–1949)") and other UN member states.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker528_152-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Tucker528-152">[148]</a></sup>

The initial Arab plans called for Syrian and Lebanese forces to invade from north while Jordanian and Iraqi forces were to invade from east in order to meet at Nazareth and then to push forward together to Haifa. In the south, the Egyptians were to advance and take Tel Aviv.<sup id="cite_ref-Gelber2006p130_156-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Gelber2006p130-156">[152]</a></sup> At the Arab League meeting in Damascus on 11–13 May, Abdullah rejected the plan, which served Syrian interests, using the fact his allies were afraid to go to war without his army. He proposed that the Iraqis attack the Jezreel valley and the Arab Legion enter Ramallah and Nablus and link with the Egyptian army at Hebron,<sup id="cite_ref-Gelber2006p130_156-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Gelber2006p130-156">[152]</a></sup> which was more in compliance with his political objective to occupy the territory allocated to the Arab State by the partition plan and promises not to invade the territory allocated to the Jewish State by the partition plan. In addition, Lebanon decided not to take part in the war at the last minute, due to the still-influential Christians' opposition and due to Jewish bribes.<sup id="cite_ref-Gelber_2006_p.11_85-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Gelber_2006_p.11-85">[81]</a></sup>

Intelligence provided by the [French consulate in Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consulate_General_of_France_in_Jerusalem "Consulate General of France in Jerusalem") on 12 May 1948 on the Arab armies' invading forces and their revised plan to invade the new state contributed to Israel's success in withstanding the Arab invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-Zamir2010p21_157-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Zamir2010p21-157">[153]</a></sup>

The first mission of the Jewish forces was to hold on against the Arab armies and stop them, although the Arabs had enjoyed major advantages (the initiative, vastly superior firepower).<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p63_158-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p63-158">[154]</a></sup> As the British stopped blocking the incoming Jewish immigrants and arms supply, the Israeli forces grew steadily with large numbers of immigrants and weapons, that allowed the Haganah to transform itself from a paramilitary force into a real army. Initially, the fighting was handled mainly by the Haganah, along with the smaller Jewish militant groups [Irgun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irgun "Irgun") and [Lehi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lehi_(group) "Lehi (group)"). On 26 May 1948, Israel established the [Israel Defense Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces "Israel Defense Forces") (IDF), incorporating these forces into one military under a central command.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

#### Southern front – Negev

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Nirim1948_1.jpg/220px-Nirim1948_1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Nirim1948_1.jpg)

Israeli soldiers in [Nirim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nirim "Nirim")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Negba1948Defenses.jpg/170px-Negba1948Defenses.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Negba1948Defenses.jpg)

Israeli soldiers in [Negba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negba "Negba")

The Egyptian force, the largest among the Arab armies, invaded from the south.

On 15 May 1948, the Egyptians attacked two settlements: [Nirim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Nirim "Battle of Nirim"), using artillery, armoured cars carrying cannons, and [Bren carriers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bren_carrier "Bren carrier");<sup id="cite_ref-morris2008p236_26-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-morris2008p236-26">[22]</a></sup> and [Kfar Darom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_Kfar_Darom "Battles of Kfar Darom")<sup id="cite_ref-morris2008p236_26-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-morris2008p236-26">[22]</a></sup> using artillery, tanks and aircraft. The Egyptians' attacks met fierce resistance from the few and lightly armed defenders of both settlements, and failed. On 19 May the Egyptians attacked [Yad Mordechai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Yad_Mordechai "Battle of Yad Mordechai"), where an inferior force of 100 Israelis armed with nothing more than rifles, a medium machinegun and a [PIAT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PIAT "PIAT") anti-tank weapon, held up a column of 2,500 Egyptians, well-supported by armour, artillery and air units, for five days.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p57_159-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p57-159">[155]</a></sup> The Egyptians took heavy losses, while the losses sustained by the defenders were comparatively light.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p56_160-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p56-160">[156]</a></sup>

One of the Egyptian force's two main columns made its way northwards along the shoreline, through what is today the [Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip") and the other column advanced eastwards toward [Beersheba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beersheba "Beersheba").<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p56_160-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p56-160">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-carta-egypt_161-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-carta-egypt-161">[157]</a></sup> To secure their flanks, the Egyptians attacked and laid siege to a number of [kibbutzim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kibbutz "Kibbutz") in the [Negev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev "Negev"), among those Kfar Darom, Nirim, Yad Mordechai, and [Negba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_Negba#First_skirmishes_and_battle_of_June_2 "Battles of Negba").<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p56_160-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p56-160">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-162">[158]</a></sup> The Israeli defenders held out fiercely for days against vastly superior forces, and managed to buy valuable time for the IDF's [Givati Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Givati_Brigade "Givati Brigade") to prepare to stop the Egyptian drive on Tel Aviv.

On 28 May the Egyptians renewed their northern advance, and stopped at a destroyed bridge north to [Isdud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashdod "Ashdod"). The Givati Brigade reported this advance but no fighters were sent to confront the Egyptians. Had the Egyptians wished to continue their advance northward, towards [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv"), there would have been no Israeli force to block them.<sup id="cite_ref-163"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-163">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-164">[160]</a></sup>

From 29 May to 3 June, Israeli forces stopped the Egyptian drive north in [Operation Pleshet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Pleshet "Operation Pleshet"). In the first combat mission performed by Israel's fledgling air force, four [Avia S-199s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avia_S-199 "Avia S-199") attacked an Egyptian armoured column of 500 vehicles on its way to [Isdud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashdod "Ashdod"). The Israeli planes dropped 70 kilogram bombs and strafed the column, although their machine guns jammed quickly. Two of the planes crashed, killing a pilot. The attack caused the Egyptians to scatter, and they had lost the initiative by the time they had regrouped. Following the air attack, Israeli forces constantly bombarded Egyptian forces in Isdud with [_Napoleonchik_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canon_de_65_M_(montagne)_modele_1906 "Canon de 65 M (montagne) modele 1906") cannons, and IDF patrols engaged in small-scale harassment of Egyptian lines. Following another air attack, the Givati Brigade launched a counterattack. Although the counterattack was repulsed, the Egyptian offensive was halted as Egypt changed its strategy from offensive to defensive, and the initiative shifted to Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-165"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-165">[161]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (June 2022)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

On 6 June, in the [Battle of Nitzanim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Nitzanim "Battle of Nitzanim"), Egyptian forces attacked the kibbutz of [Nitzanim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitzanim "Nitzanim"), located between [Majdal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Majdal,_Askalan "Al-Majdal, Askalan") and [Isdud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isdud "Isdud"), and the Israeli defenders surrendered after resisting for five days.

#### Battles of Latrun

The heaviest fighting occurred in [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_for_Jerusalem_(1948) "Battle for Jerusalem (1948)") and on the Jerusalem – Tel Aviv road, between Jordan's [Arab Legion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Legion "Arab Legion") and Israeli forces.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p61-62_166-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p61-62-166">[162]</a></sup> As part of the redeployment to deal with the Egyptian advance, the Israelis abandoned the Latrun fortress overlooking the main highway to Jerusalem, which the Arab Legion immediately seized.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p61_167-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p61-167">[163]</a></sup> The Arab Legion also occupied the Latrun Monastery. From these positions, the Jordanians were able to cut off supplies to Israeli fighters and civilians in Jerusalem.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p62_168-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p62-168">[164]</a></sup>

The Israelis attempted to take the Latrun fortress in a series of battles lasting from 24 May to 18 July. The Arab Legion held Latrun and managed to repulse the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p62_168-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p62-168">[164]</a></sup> During the attempts to take Latrun, Israeli forces suffered some 586 casualties, among them [Mickey Marcus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mickey_Marcus "Mickey Marcus"), Israel's first general, who was killed by [friendly fire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friendly_fire "Friendly fire"). The Arab Legion also took losses, losing 90 dead and some 200 wounded up to 29 May.<sup id="cite_ref-169"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-169">[165]</a></sup>

-   [![Building the Burma Road](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Handasa-burma001.jpg/240px-Handasa-burma001.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Handasa-burma001.jpg "Building the Burma Road")
    
    Building the Burma Road
    
-   [![A bulldozer tows a truck on the "Burma road", June 1948](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Burma_Road_1948.jpg/240px-Burma_Road_1948.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Burma_Road_1948.jpg "A bulldozer tows a truck on the "Burma road", June 1948")
    
    A bulldozer tows a truck on the "Burma road", June 1948
    
-   [![Area map](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Latroun_%2811_juin%29.png/240px-Latroun_%2811_juin%29.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Latroun_(11_juin).png "Area map")
    
    Area map
    

The besieged Israeli [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem") was only saved via the opening of the so-called "[Burma Road](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burma_Road_(Israel) "Burma Road (Israel)")", a makeshift bypass road built by Israeli forces that allowed Israeli supply convoys to pass into Jerusalem.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p62_168-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p62-168">[164]</a></sup> Parts of the area where the road was built were cleared of Jordanian snipers in May and the road was completed on 14 June. Supplies had already begun passing through before the road was completed, with the first convoy passing through on the night of 1–2 June. The Jordanians spotted the activity and attempted to shell the road, but were ineffective, as it could not be seen. However, Jordanian sharpshooters killed several road workers, and an attack on 9 June left eight Israelis dead. On 18 July, elements of the [Harel Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harel_Brigade "Harel Brigade") took about 10 villages to the south of Latrun to enlarge and secure the area of the Burma Road.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

The Arab Legion was able to repel an Israeli attack on Latrun. The Jordanians launched two counterattacks, temporarily taking [Beit Susin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beit_Susin "Beit Susin") before being forced back, and capturing [Gezer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gezer_(kibbutz) "Gezer (kibbutz)") after a fierce battle, which was retaken by two Palmach squads the same evening.<sup id="cite_ref-170"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-170">[166]</a></sup>

-   [![Jordanian artillery shelling Jerusalem in 1948](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/1948-Jordanian_artillery_shelling_Jerusalem.jpg/232px-1948-Jordanian_artillery_shelling_Jerusalem.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1948-Jordanian_artillery_shelling_Jerusalem.jpg "Jordanian artillery shelling Jerusalem in 1948")
    
    Jordanian artillery shelling Jerusalem in 1948
    
-   [![Arab Legion soldier standing in ruins of the most sacred Synagogue, the "Hurva", Old City.[167]](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Arab_Legion_soldier_in_ruins_of_Hurva.jpg/201px-Arab_Legion_soldier_in_ruins_of_Hurva.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Arab_Legion_soldier_in_ruins_of_Hurva.jpg "Arab Legion soldier standing in ruins of the most sacred Synagogue, the "Hurva", Old City.[167]")
    
    [Arab Legion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Legion "Arab Legion") soldier standing in ruins of the most sacred Synagogue, the ["Hurva"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hurva_Synagogue "Hurva Synagogue"), [Old City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_City_(Jerusalem) "Old City (Jerusalem)").<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p218_171-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p218-171">[167]</a></sup>
    
-   [![Jewish residents of Jerusalem fleeing during the battle for the Old City](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Jewish_Quarter_Refugees.jpg/135px-Jewish_Quarter_Refugees.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jewish_Quarter_Refugees.jpg "Jewish residents of Jerusalem fleeing during the battle for the Old City")
    
    Jewish residents of Jerusalem fleeing during the battle for the [Old City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_City_(Jerusalem) "Old City (Jerusalem)")
    

#### Battle for Jerusalem

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Prof_Fekete_Rector_Heb_Uni-water-allocation.jpg/130px-Prof_Fekete_Rector_Heb_Uni-water-allocation.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Prof_Fekete_Rector_Heb_Uni-water-allocation.jpg)

Mathematics professor [Michael Fekete](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Fekete "Michael Fekete"), the [Provost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provost_(education) "Provost (education)") of the [Hebrew University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_University "Hebrew University") of [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem"), with his water quota, during the siege of [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem")

The Jordanians in [Latrun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latrun "Latrun") cut off supplies to western Jerusalem.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p62_168-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p62-168">[164]</a></sup> Though some supplies, mostly munitions, were airdropped into the city, the shortage of food, water, fuel and medicine was acute. The Israeli forces were seriously short of food, water and ammunition.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p62_168-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p62-168">[164]</a></sup>

King Abdullah ordered [Glubb Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Bagot_Glubb "John Bagot Glubb"), the commander of the Arab Legion, to enter Jerusalem on 17 May. The Arab Legion fired 10,000 artillery and mortar shells a day,<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p62_168-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p62-168">[164]</a></sup> and also attacked [West Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Jerusalem "West Jerusalem") with sniper fire.

Heavy house-to-house fighting occurred between 19 and 28 May, with the Arab Legion eventually succeeding in pushing Israeli forces from the Arab neighbourhoods of Jerusalem as well as the [Jewish Quarter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_Quarter_(Jerusalem) "Jewish Quarter (Jerusalem)") of the Old City.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p62_168-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p62-168">[164]</a></sup> The 1,500 Jewish inhabitants of the Old City's Jewish Quarter were expelled, and several hundred were detained. The Jews had to be escorted out by the Arab Legion to protect them against Palestinian Arab mobs that intended to massacre them.<sup id="cite_ref-172"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-172">[168]</a></sup>

On 22 May, Arab forces attacked kibbutz [Ramat Rachel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramat_Rachel "Ramat Rachel") south of Jerusalem. After a fierce battle in which 31 Jordanians and 13 Israelis were killed, the defenders of Ramat Rachel withdrew, only to partially retake the kibbutz the following day. Fighting continued until 26 May, until the entire kibbutz was recaptured. [Radar Hill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Har_Adar "Har Adar") was also taken from the Arab Legion, and held until 26 May, when the Jordanians retook it in a battle that left 19 Israelis and 2 Jordanians dead.<sup id="cite_ref-title=Netanel_Lorch_1961_p.192_173-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-title=Netanel_Lorch_1961_p.192-173">[169]</a></sup> A total of 23 attempts by the [Harel Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harel_Brigade "Harel Brigade") to capture Radar Hill in the war failed.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

The same day, [Thomas C. Wasson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_C._Wasson "Thomas C. Wasson"), the [US Consul-General in Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consulate_General_of_the_United_States,_Jerusalem "Consulate General of the United States, Jerusalem") and a member of the UN Truce Commission was shot dead in West Jerusalem. It was disputed whether Wasson was killed by the Arabs or Israelis.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

In mid to late October 1948, the [Harel Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harel_Brigade "Harel Brigade") began its offensive in what was known as [Operation Ha-Har](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Ha-Har "Operation Ha-Har"), to secure the [Jerusalem Corridor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem_Corridor "Jerusalem Corridor").<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

#### Northern Samaria

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Afulahagana.jpg/220px-Afulahagana.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Afulahagana.jpg)

Israeli soldiers in [Afula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afula "Afula")

An Iraqi force consisting of two infantry and one armoured brigade crossed the Jordan River from northern Jordan, [attacking the Israeli settlement of Gesher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gesher,_Israel#1948_Israeli-Arab_war "Gesher, Israel") with little success.<sup id="cite_ref-morris2008p236_26-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-morris2008p236-26">[22]</a></sup> Following this defeat, Iraqi forces moved into the strategic triangle bounded by the Arab towns [Nablus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nablus "Nablus"), [Jenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jenin "Jenin") and [Tulkarm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tulkarm "Tulkarm"). On 25 May, they were making their way towards [Netanya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netanya "Netanya"), when they were stopped.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p60_174-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p60-174">[170]</a></sup> On 29 May, an Israeli attack against the Iraqis led to three days of heavy fighting over Jenin, but Iraqi forces managed to hold their positions.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p60_174-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p60-174">[170]</a></sup> After these battles, the Iraqi forces became stationary and their involvement in the war effectively ended.<sup id="cite_ref-Pollack149-155_135-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Pollack149-155-135">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p60_174-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p60-174">[170]</a></sup>

Iraqi forces failed in their attacks on Israeli settlements with the most notable battle taking place at [Gesher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gesher,_Israel "Gesher, Israel"), and instead took defensive positions around [Jenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jenin "Jenin"), [Nablus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nablus "Nablus"), and [Tulkarm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tulkarm "Tulkarm"), from where they could put pressure on the Israeli center.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-175"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-175">[171]</a></sup> On 25 May, Iraqi forces advanced from Tulkarm, taking [Geulim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geulim "Geulim") and reaching [Kfar Yona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kfar_Yona "Kfar Yona") and [Ein Vered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ein_Vered "Ein Vered") on the Tulkarm-[Netanya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netanya "Netanya") road. The [Alexandroni Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexandroni_Brigade "Alexandroni Brigade") then stopped the Iraqi advance and retook Geulim. The IDF [Carmeli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carmeli_Brigade "Carmeli Brigade") and [Golani Brigades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golani_Brigade "Golani Brigade") attempted to capture Jenin during an offensive launched on 31 May, but were defeated in course of the subsequent [battle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Jenin_(1948) "Battle of Jenin (1948)") by an Iraqi counterattack.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

#### Northern front – Lake of Galilee

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Deganiatank1.jpg/220px-Deganiatank1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Deganiatank1.jpg)

Syrian [R-35](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renault_R35 "Renault R35") [light tank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_tank "Light tank") destroyed at [Degania Alef](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Degania_Alef "Degania Alef")

On 14 May Syria entered Palestine with the 1st Infantry Brigade supported by a battalion of armoured cars, a company of French [R 35](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renault_R35 "Renault R35") and R 37 tanks, an artillery battalion and other units.<sup id="cite_ref-pollack2002p448-457_176-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-pollack2002p448-457-176">[172]</a></sup> The Syrian president, [Shukri al-Quwwatli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shukri_al-Quwwatli "Shukri al-Quwwatli") instructed his troops in the front, "to destroy the Zionists". "The situation was very grave. There aren't enough rifles. There are no heavy weapons," [Ben-Gurion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion "David Ben-Gurion") told the Israeli Cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-177"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-177">[173]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tal,_2004,_pp._251_178-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Tal,_2004,_pp._251-178">[174]</a></sup> On 15 May, the Syrian forces turned to the eastern and southern [Sea of Galilee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_of_Galilee "Sea of Galilee") shores, and attacked [Samakh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samakh,_Tiberias "Samakh, Tiberias") the neighbouring [Tegart fort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tegart_fort "Tegart fort") and the settlements of [Sha'ar HaGolan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sha%27ar_HaGolan "Sha'ar HaGolan"), [Ein Gev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ein_Gev "Ein Gev"), but they were bogged down by resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-morris2008p236_26-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-morris2008p236-26">[22]</a></sup> Later, they attacked [Samakh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samakh,_Tiberias "Samakh, Tiberias") using tanks and aircraft, and on 18 May they succeeded in conquering [Samakh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samakh,_Tiberias "Samakh, Tiberias")<sup id="cite_ref-pollack2002p448-457_176-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-pollack2002p448-457-176">[172]</a></sup> and occupied the abandoned [Sha'ar HaGolan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sha%27ar_HaGolan "Sha'ar HaGolan").<sup id="cite_ref-morris2008p236_26-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-morris2008p236-26">[22]</a></sup>

On 21 May, the Syrian army was stopped at kibbutz [Degania Alef](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_the_Kinarot_Valley "Battles of the Kinarot Valley") in the north, where local militia reinforced by elements of the [Carmeli Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carmeli_Brigade "Carmeli Brigade") halted Syrian armoured forces with [Molotov cocktails](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molotov_cocktail "Molotov cocktail"), hand grenades and a single [PIAT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PIAT "PIAT"). One tank that was disabled by Molotov cocktails and hand grenades still remains at the kibbutz. The remaining Syrian forces were driven off the next day by four [Napoleonchik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonchik "Napoleonchik") mountain guns – Israel's first use of artillery during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-179"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-179">[175]</a></sup> Following the Syrian forces' defeat at the [Deganias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Degania_Alef "Degania Alef") a few days later, they abandoned the [Samakh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samakh,_Tiberias "Samakh, Tiberias") village.<sup id="cite_ref-pollack2002p448-457_176-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-pollack2002p448-457-176">[172]</a></sup> The Syrians were forced to besiege the kibbutz rather than advance.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p60_174-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p60-174">[170]</a></sup> One author claims that the main reason for the Syrian defeat was the Syrian soldiers' low regard for the Israelis who they believed would not stand and fight against the Arab army.<sup id="cite_ref-Tal,_2004,_pp._251_178-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Tal,_2004,_pp._251-178">[174]</a></sup>

On 6 June, the 3rd battalion of the [Lebanese Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanese_Armed_Forces "Lebanese Armed Forces") took [Al-Malkiyya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Malkiyya "Al-Malkiyya") and [Qadas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qadas "Qadas") in what became the only intervention of the Lebanese army during the war, handing the towns over to the [Arab Liberation Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Liberation_Army "Arab Liberation Army") and withdrawing on 8 July.<sup id="cite_ref-Hughes_15-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Hughes-15">[12]</a></sup>

On 6 June, Syrian forces attacked Mishmar HaYarden, but they were repulsed. On 10 June, the Syrians overran [Mishmar HaYarden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mishmar_HaYarden "Mishmar HaYarden") and advanced to the main road, where they were stopped by units of the [Oded Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oded_Brigade "Oded Brigade").<sup id="cite_ref-180"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-180">[176]</a></sup> Subsequently, the Syrians reverted to a defensive posture, conducting only a few minor attacks on small, exposed Israeli settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-pollack2002p448-457_176-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-pollack2002p448-457-176">[172]</a></sup>

#### Palestinian forces

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/PikiWiki_Israel_20772_The_Palmach.jpg/170px-PikiWiki_Israel_20772_The_Palmach.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_20772_The_Palmach.jpg)

Kaukji, the [Arab Liberation Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Liberation_Army "Arab Liberation Army") commander

In the continuity of the civil war between Jewish and Arab forces that had begun in 1947, battles between Israeli forces and Palestinian Arab militias took place, particularly in the Lydda, al-Ramla, Jerusalem, and Haifa areas. On 23 May, the [Alexandroni Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexandroni_Brigade "Alexandroni Brigade") captured [Tantura](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tantura "Tantura"), south of [Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa"), from Arab forces. On 2 June, Holy War Army commander [Hasan Salama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasan_Salama "Hasan Salama") was killed in a battle with Haganah at [Ras al-Ein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ras_al-Ein "Ras al-Ein").<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

#### Air operations

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Egyptian_Plane_TA_1948.jpg/220px-Egyptian_Plane_TA_1948.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Egyptian_Plane_TA_1948.jpg)

An Egyptian [Spitfire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire "Supermarine Spitfire") shot down over Tel Aviv on 15 May 1948

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Egyptian_bombing_1948.jpg/220px-Egyptian_bombing_1948.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Egyptian_bombing_1948.jpg)

Volunteers evacuating a wounded man during Egyptian bombardment of Tel Aviv.

All Jewish aviation assets were placed under the control of the _[Sherut Avir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sherut_Avir "Sherut Avir")_ (Air Service, known as the SA) in November 1947 and flying operations began in the following month from a small civil airport on the outskirts of [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv") called [Sde Dov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sde_Dov_Airport "Sde Dov Airport"), with the first ground support operation (in an [RWD-13](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RWD-13 "RWD-13"))<sup id="cite_ref-181"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-181">[177]</a></sup> taking place on 17 December. The [Galilee Squadron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galilee_Squadron "Galilee Squadron") was formed at [Yavne'el](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yavne%27el "Yavne'el") in March 1948, and the Negev Squadron was formed at [Nir-Am](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nir-Am "Nir-Am") in April. By 10 May, when the SA suffered its first combat loss, there were three flying units, an air staff, maintenance facilities and logistics support. At the outbreak of the war on 15 May, the SA became the [Israeli Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force "Israeli Air Force"). With its fleet<sup id="cite_ref-182"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-182">[178]</a></sup> of light planes it was no match for Arab forces during the first few weeks of the war with their [T-6s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T-6_Texan "T-6 Texan"), [Spitfires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spitfire "Spitfire"), [C-47s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C-47 "C-47"), and [Avro Ansons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avro_Anson "Avro Anson").

On 15 May, with the beginning of the war, four [Royal Egyptian Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Egyptian_Air_Force "Royal Egyptian Air Force") (REAF) Spitfires attacked [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv"), bombing [Sde Dov Airfield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sde_Dov_Airport "Sde Dov Airport"), where the bulk of Sherut Avir's aircraft were concentrated, as well as the [Reading Power Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reading_Power_Station "Reading Power Station"). Several aircraft were destroyed, some others were damaged, and five Israelis were killed. Throughout the following hours, additional waves of Egyptian aircraft bombed and strafed targets around Tel Aviv, although these raids had little effect. One Spitfire was shot down by anti-aircraft fire, and its pilot was taken prisoner.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris_2008,_p._261_183-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris_2008,_p._261-183">[179]</a></sup>

Throughout the next six days, the REAF continued to attack Tel Aviv, causing civilian casualties. On 18 May, Egyptian warplanes attacked the [Tel Aviv Central Bus Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv_Central_Bus_Station "Tel Aviv Central Bus Station"), killing 42 people and wounding 100. In addition to their attacks on Tel Aviv, the Egyptians bombed rural settlements and airfields, though few casualties were caused in these raids.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris_2008,_p._261_183-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris_2008,_p._261-183">[179]</a></sup>

At the outset of the war, the REAF was able to attack Israel with near impunity, due to the lack of Israeli fighter aircraft to intercept them,<sup id="cite_ref-184"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-184">[180]</a></sup> and met only ground fire.

As more effective air defences were transferred to Tel Aviv, the Egyptians began taking significant aircraft losses. As a result of these losses, as well as the loss of five Spitfires downed by the British when the Egyptians mistakenly attacked [RAF Ramat David](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramat_David_Airbase "Ramat David Airbase"), the Egyptian air attacks became less frequent. By the end of May 1948, almost the entire REAF Spitfire squadron based in [El Arish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Arish "El Arish") had been lost, including many of its best pilots.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

Although lacking fighter or bomber aircraft, in the first few days of the war, Israel's embryonic air force still attacked Arab targets, with light aircraft being utilised as makeshift bombers, striking Arab encampments and columns. The raids were mostly carried out at night to avoid interception by Arab fighter aircraft. These attacks usually had little effect, except on morale.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Avia-S-199-IAF-101Sqn-Tel-Nof-Israel-1948-01.jpg/220px-Avia-S-199-IAF-101Sqn-Tel-Nof-Israel-1948-01.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Avia-S-199-IAF-101Sqn-Tel-Nof-Israel-1948-01.jpg)

An Avia S-199, Israel's 1st fighter aircraft

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Spitfire-MkIX-hatzerim-1-2.jpg/220px-Spitfire-MkIX-hatzerim-1-2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Spitfire-MkIX-hatzerim-1-2.jpg)

An Israeli Spitfire F Mk

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Israeli_B-17Gs_01011953.JPG/170px-Israeli_B-17Gs_01011953.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Israeli_B-17Gs_01011953.JPG)

Israeli B-17s in flight

The balance of air power soon began to swing in favour of the Israeli Air Force following the arrival of 25 [Avia S-199s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avia_S-199 "Avia S-199") from [Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovakia "Czechoslovakia"), the first of which arrived in Israel on 20 May. Ironically, Israel was using the Avia S-199, an inferior derivative of the [Bf 109](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Messerschmitt_Bf_109 "Messerschmitt Bf 109") designed in [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") to counter British-designed Spitfires flown by Egypt. Throughout the rest of the war, Israel would acquire more Avia fighters, as well as 62 Spitfires from Czechoslovakia. On 28 May 1948, Sherut Avir became the Israeli Air Force.<sup id="cite_ref-185"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-185">[181]</a></sup>

Many of the pilots who fought for the Israeli Air Force were [foreign volunteers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahal_(Israel) "Mahal (Israel)") or mercenaries, including many [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II") veterans.<sup id="cite_ref-David_Bercuson_1984_p.74_186-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-David_Bercuson_1984_p.74-186">[182]</a></sup>

On 3 June, Israel scored its first victory in aerial combat when Israeli pilot [Modi Alon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modi_Alon "Modi Alon") shot down a pair of Egyptian DC-3s that had just bombed Tel Aviv. Although Tel Aviv would see additional raids by fighter aircraft, there would be no more raids by bombers for the rest of the war. From then on, the [Israeli Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force "Israeli Air Force") began engaging the Arab air forces in air-to-air combat. The first dogfight took place on 8 June, when an Israeli fighter plane flown by Gideon Lichtman shot down an Egyptian Spitfire. By the fall of 1948, the IAF had achieved [air superiority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_superiority "Air superiority") and had superior firepower and more knowledgeable personnel, many of whom had seen action in World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-187"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-187">[183]</a></sup> Israeli planes then began intercepting and engaging Arab aircraft on bombing missions.

Following Israeli air attacks on Egyptian and Iraqi columns, the Egyptians repeatedly bombed [Ekron Airfield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Nof_Airbase "Tel Nof Airbase"), where IAF fighters were based. During a 30 May raid, bombs aimed for Ekron hit central [Rehovot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rehovot "Rehovot"), killing 7 civilians and wounding 30. In response to this, and probably to the Jordanian victories at [Latrun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_Latrun_(1948) "Battles of Latrun (1948)"), Israel began bombing targets in Arab cities. On the night of 31 May/1 June, the first Israeli raid on an Arab capital took place when three IAF planes flew to [Amman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amman "Amman") and dropped several dozen 55 and 110-pound bombs, hitting the King's Palace and an adjacent British airfield. Some 12 people were killed and 30 wounded. During the attack, an RAF hangar was damaged, as were some British aircraft. The British threatened that in the event of another such attack, they would shoot down the attacking aircraft and bomb Israeli airfields, and as a result, Israeli aircraft did not attack Amman again for the rest of the war. Israel also bombed [Arish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arish "Arish"), [Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_City "Gaza City"), [Damascus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damascus "Damascus"), and [Cairo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cairo "Cairo"). Israeli [Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boeing_B-17_Flying_Fortress "Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress") bombers flying to Israel from [Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovakia "Czechoslovakia") bombed Egypt on their way.<sup id="cite_ref-188"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-188">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-189">[185]</a></sup>

#### Sea battles

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Northland_Color_1.jpg/220px-Northland_Color_1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Northland_Color_1.jpg)

_Northland_ in [Greenland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenland "Greenland") _circa_ 1944 which became the Israeli INS Eilat

At the outset of the war, the [Israeli Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Navy "Israeli Navy") consisted of three former [Aliyah Bet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah_Bet "Aliyah Bet") ships that had been seized by the British and impounded in [Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa") harbour, where they were tied up at the breakwater. Work on establishing a navy had begun shortly before Israeli independence, and the three ships were selected due to them having a military background – one, the INS _Eilat_, was an ex-[US Coast Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard "United States Coast Guard") icebreaker, and the other two, the INS _Haganah_ and INS _Wedgwood_, had been [Royal Canadian Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Navy "Royal Canadian Navy") corvettes.<sup id="cite_ref-navy_190-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-navy-190">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gershoni,_pp._46–47_191-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Gershoni,_pp._46%E2%80%9347-191">[187]</a></sup>

The ships were put into minimum running condition by contractors dressed as stevedores and port personnel, who were able to work in the engine rooms and below deck. The work had to be clandestine to avoid arousing British suspicion. On 21 May 1948, the three ships set sail for Tel Aviv, and were made to look like ships that had been purchased by foreign owners for commercial use. In Tel Aviv, the ships were fitted with small field guns dating to the late 19th century and anti-aircraft guns.<sup id="cite_ref-navy_190-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-navy-190">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gershoni,_pp._46–47_191-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Gershoni,_pp._46%E2%80%9347-191">[187]</a></sup>

After the British left Haifa port on 30 June, Haifa became the main base of the Israeli Navy. In October 1948, a [submarine chaser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Submarine_chaser "Submarine chaser") was purchased from the United States. The warships were manned by former merchant seamen, former crewmembers of Aliyah Bet ships, Israelis who had served in the [Royal Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Navy "Royal Navy") during World War II, and foreign volunteers. The newly refurbished and crewed warships served on coastal patrol duties and bombarded Egyptian coastal installations in and around the [Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_City "Gaza City") area all the way to [Port Said](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_Said "Port Said").<sup id="cite_ref-navy_190-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-navy-190">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gershoni,_pp._46–47_191-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Gershoni,_pp._46%E2%80%9347-191">[187]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (June 2022)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

#### End of the first phase

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Palestine_Military_Situation%2C_June_11%2C_1948%2C_Truman_Papers.jpg/220px-Palestine_Military_Situation%2C_June_11%2C_1948%2C_Truman_Papers.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Palestine_Military_Situation,_June_11,_1948,_Truman_Papers.jpg)

The Palestine Military Situation, 11 June 1948. Truman Papers

Throughout the following days, the Arabs were only able to make limited gains due to fierce Israeli resistance, and were quickly driven off their new holdings by Israeli counterattacks.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

As the war progressed, the IDF managed to field more troops than the Arab forces. In July 1948, the IDF had 63,000 troops; by early spring 1949, they had 115,000. The Arab armies had an estimated 40,000 troops in July 1948, rising to 55,000 in October 1948, and slightly more by the spring of 1949.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

Upon the implementation of the truce, the IDF had control over nine Arab cities and towns or mixed cities and towns: New [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem"), [Jaffa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaffa "Jaffa"), [Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa"), [Acre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acre,_Israel "Acre, Israel"), [Safed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safed "Safed"), [Tiberias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiberias "Tiberias"), [Baysan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baysan "Baysan") (Beit She'an), [Samakh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samakh,_Tiberias "Samakh, Tiberias") and [Yibna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yibna "Yibna") ([Yavne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yavne "Yavne")). Another city, [Jenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jenin "Jenin"), was not occupied but its residents fled. The combined Arab forces captured 14 Jewish settlement points, but only one of them, [Mishmar HaYarden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mishmar_HaYarden "Mishmar HaYarden"), was in the territory of the proposed Jewish State according to [Resolution 181](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine "United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine").<sup id="cite_ref-statsgelber_192-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-statsgelber-192">[188]</a></sup>

Within the boundaries of the proposed Jewish state, there were twelve Arab villages which opposed Jewish control or were captured by the invading Arab armies, and in addition to them, the [Lod Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lod_Airport "Lod Airport") and pumping station near [Antipatris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antipatris "Antipatris"), which were within the boundaries of the proposed Jewish state, were under the control of the Arabs. The IDF captured about 50 large Arab villages outside of the boundaries of the proposed Jewish State and a larger number of hamlets and Bedouin encampments. 350 square kilometres of the proposed Jewish State were under the control of the Arab forces, while 700 square kilometres of the proposed Arab State were under the control of the IDF. This figure ignores the Negev desert which was not under any absolute control of either side.<sup id="cite_ref-statsgelber_192-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-statsgelber-192">[188]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2021)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

In the period between the invasion and the first truce the Syrian army had 315 of its men killed and 400–500 injured; the Iraqi expeditionary force had 200 of its men killed and 500 injured; the Jordanian Arab Legion had 300 of its men killed and 400–500 (including irregulars and Palesinian volunteers fighting under the Jordanians); the Egyptian army had 600 of its men killed and 1,400 injured (including irregulars from the [Muslim Brotherhood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood "Muslim Brotherhood")); the ALA, which returned to fight in early June, had 100 of its men killed or injured. 800 Jews were taken hostage by the Arabs and 1,300 Arabs were taken hostage by the Jews, mostly Palestinians.<sup id="cite_ref-statsgelber_192-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-statsgelber-192">[188]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2021)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

### First truce: 11 June – 8 July 1948

The UN declared a truce on 29 May, which came into effect on 11 June and lasted 28 days. The truce was designed to last 28 days and an arms embargo was declared with the intention that neither side would make any gains from the truce. Neither side respected the truce; both found ways around the restrictions placed on them.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p64_193-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p64-193">[189]</a></sup> Both the Israelis and the Arabs used this time to improve their positions, a direct violation of the terms of the ceasefire.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p269_194-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p269-194">[190]</a></sup>

#### Reinforcements

<table><caption>Israeli Forces 1948<sup id="cite_ref-195"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-195">[191]</a></sup></caption><tbody><tr><td>Initial strength</td><td>29,677</td></tr><tr><td>4 June</td><td>40,825</td></tr><tr><td>17 July</td><td>63,586</td></tr><tr><td>7 October</td><td>88,033</td></tr><tr><td>28 October</td><td>92,275</td></tr><tr><td>2 December</td><td>106,900</td></tr><tr><td>23 December</td><td>107,652</td></tr><tr><td>30 December</td><td>108,300</td></tr></tbody></table>

At the time of the truce, the British view was that "the Jews are too weak in armament to achieve spectacular success".<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p64_193-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p64-193">[189]</a></sup> As the truce commenced, a British officer stationed in [Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa") stated that the four-week-long truce "would certainly be exploited by the Jews to continue military training and reorganization while the Arabs would waste \[them\] feuding over the future divisions of the spoils".<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p269_194-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p269-194">[190]</a></sup> During the truce, the Israelis sought to bolster their forces by massive import of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p64_193-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p64-193">[189]</a></sup> The IDF was able to [acquire weapons from Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arms_shipments_from_Czechoslovakia_to_Israel_1947%E2%80%931949 "Arms shipments from Czechoslovakia to Israel 1947–1949") as well as improve training of forces and reorganisation of the army during this time. [Yitzhak Rabin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin "Yitzhak Rabin"), an IDF commander at the time of the war and later Israel's fifth Prime Minister, stated "\[w\]ithout the arms from Czechoslovakia... it is very doubtful whether we would have been able to conduct the war".<sup id="cite_ref-196"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-196">[192]</a></sup>

The Israeli army increased its manpower from approximately 30,000–35,000 men to almost 65,000 during the truce due to mobilisation and the constant immigration into Israel. It was also able to increase its arms supply to more than 25,000 rifles, 5,000 machine guns, and fifty million bullets.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p269_194-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p269-194">[190]</a></sup> As well as violating the arms and personnel embargo, they also sent fresh units to the front lines, much as their Arab enemies did.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p269_194-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p269-194">[190]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Altalena_off_Tel-Aviv_beach.jpg/220px-Altalena_off_Tel-Aviv_beach.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Altalena_off_Tel-Aviv_beach.jpg)

_Altalena_ burning near Tel Aviv beach

During the truce, Irgun attempted to bring in a private arms shipment aboard a ship called _[Altalena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altalena_Affair "Altalena Affair")_. Fearing a coup by the Irgun (at the time the IDF was in the process of integrating various pre-independence political factions), Ben-Gurion ordered that the arms be confiscated by force. After some miscommunication, the army was ordered by Ben-Gurion to sink the ship. Sixteen Irgun members and three IDF soldiers were killed in the fighting.<sup id="cite_ref-Dov_Joseph_1960_p.239_197-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Dov_Joseph_1960_p.239-197">[193]</a></sup>

#### UN mediator Bernadotte

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Folke-Bernadotte.jpg/170px-Folke-Bernadotte.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Folke-Bernadotte.jpg)

UN Palestine mediator, [Folke Bernadotte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folke_Bernadotte "Folke Bernadotte"), assassinated in September 1948 by the militant group [Lehi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lehi_(group) "Lehi (group)")

The [ceasefire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceasefire "Ceasefire") was overseen by UN mediator [Folke Bernadotte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folke_Bernadotte "Folke Bernadotte") and a team of UN Observers made up of army officers from Belgium, United States, Sweden and France.<sup id="cite_ref-198"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-198">[194]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (June 2022)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Bernadotte was voted in by the General Assembly to "assure the safety of the holy places, to safeguard the well-being of the population, and to promote 'a peaceful adjustment of the future situation of Palestine'".<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p269_194-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p269-194">[190]</a></sup> [Folke Bernadotte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folke_Bernadotte "Folke Bernadotte") reported:

> During the period of the truce, three violations occurred ... of such a serious nature:
> 
> 1.  the attempt by ...the Irgun Zvai Leumi to bring war materials and immigrants, including men of military age, into Palestine aboard the ship _Altalena_ on 21 June...
> 2.  Another truce violation occurred through the refusal of Egyptian forces to permit the passage of relief convoys to Jewish settlements in the Negeb...
> 3.  The third violation of the truce arose as a result of the failure of the Transjordan and Iraqi forces to permit the flow of water to Jerusalem.<sup id="cite_ref-BernadotteViolations_199-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-BernadotteViolations-199">[195]</a></sup>

After the truce was in place, Bernadotte began to address the issue of achieving a political settlement. The main obstacles in his opinion were "the Arab world's continued rejection of the existence of a Jewish state, whatever its borders; Israel's new 'philosophy', based on its increasing military strength, of ignoring the partition boundaries and conquering what additional territory it could; and the emerging Palestinian Arab refugee problem".<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p269_194-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p269-194">[190]</a></sup>

Taking all the issues into account, Bernadotte presented a new partition plan. He proposed there be a Palestinian Arab state alongside Israel and that a "Union" "be established between the two sovereign states of Israel and Jordan (which now included the West Bank); that the Negev, or part of it, be included in the Arab state and that Western Galilee, or part of it, be included in Israel; that the whole of Jerusalem be part of the Arab state, with the Jewish areas enjoying municipal autonomy and that Lydda Airport and Haifa be 'free ports' – presumably free of Israeli or Arab sovereignty".<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p269_194-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p269-194">[190]</a></sup> Israel rejected the proposal, in particular the aspect of losing control of Jerusalem, but they did agree to extend the truce for another month. The Arabs rejected both the extension of the truce and the proposal.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p269_194-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p269-194">[190]</a></sup>

### Second phase: 8–18 July 1948 ("Ten Day Battles")

On 8 July, the day before the expiration of the truce, Egyptian forces under General [Muhammad Naguib](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Naguib "Muhammad Naguib") renewed the war by [attacking Negba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_Negba#Battle_of_July_12 "Battles of Negba").<sup id="cite_ref-Knopf330_200-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Knopf330-200">[196]</a></sup> The following day, Israeli air forces launched a simultaneous offensive on all three fronts, ranging from [Quneitra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quneitra "Quneitra") to [Arish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arish "Arish") and the Egyptian air force bombed the city of Tel Aviv.<sup id="cite_ref-201"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-201">[197]</a></sup> During the fighting, the Israelis were able to open a lifeline to a number of besieged kibbutzim.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p64_193-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p64-193">[189]</a></sup>

The fighting continued for ten days until the UN Security Council issued the Second Truce on 18 July. During those 10 days, the fighting was dominated by large-scale Israeli offensives and a defensive posture from the Arab side.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

#### Southern front

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/6pdr-Aibdis.jpg/220px-6pdr-Aibdis.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:6pdr-Aibdis.jpg)

An Egyptian artillery piece captured by battalion 53 of the [Givati Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Givati_Brigade "Givati Brigade").

In the south, the IDF carried out several offensives, including [Operation An-Far](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_An-Far "Operation An-Far") and [Operation Death to the Invader](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Death_to_the_Invader "Operation Death to the Invader"). The task of the 11th Brigades's 1st Battalion on the southern flank was to capture villages, and its operation ran smoothly, with but little resistance from local irregulars. According to Amnon Neumann, a [Palmach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palmach "Palmach") veteran of the Southern front, hardly any Arab villages in the south fought back, due to the miserable poverty of their means and lack of weapons, and suffered expulsion.<sup id="cite_ref-202"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-202">[198]</a></sup> What slight resistance was offered was quelled by an artillery barrage, followed by the storming of the village, whose residents were expelled and houses destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-203"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-203">[199]</a></sup>

On 12 July, the Egyptians launched an offensive action, and again attacked [Negba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negba "Negba"), which they had previously failed to capture, using three infantry battalions, an armoured battalion, and an artillery regiment. In the battle that followed, the Egyptians were repulsed, suffering 200–300 casualties, while the Israelis lost 5 dead and 16 wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-204"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-204">[200]</a></sup>

After failing to take Negba, the Egyptians turned their attention to more isolated settlements and positions. On 14 July, an Egyptian attack on [Gal On](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gal_On "Gal On") was driven off by a minefield and by resistance from Gal On's residents.<sup id="cite_ref-205"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-205">[201]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2021)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

The Egyptians then assaulted the lightly defended village of [Be'erot Yitzhak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Be%27erot_Yitzhak "Be'erot Yitzhak"). The Egyptians managed to penetrate the village perimeter, but the defenders concentrated in an inner position in the village and fought off the Egyptian advance until IDF reinforcements arrived and drove out the attackers. The Egyptians suffered an estimated 200 casualties, while the Israelis had 17 dead and 15 wounded. The battle was one of Egypt's last offensive actions during the war, and the Egyptians did not attack any Israeli villages following this battle.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

#### Lydda and al-Ramla

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/IDFSoldierInLyddaOrRamla.png/220px-IDFSoldierInLyddaOrRamla.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IDFSoldierInLyddaOrRamla.png)

Israeli soldiers in Lod (Lydda) or Ramle

On 10 July, [Glubb Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glubb_Pasha "Glubb Pasha") ordered the defending [Arab Legion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Legion "Arab Legion") troops to "make arrangements...for a phony war".<sup id="cite_ref-206"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-206">[202]</a></sup> Israeli [Operation Danny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Danny "Operation Danny") was the most important Israeli offensive, aimed at securing and enlarging the corridor between Jerusalem and Tel Aviv by capturing the roadside cities [Lod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lod "Lod") (Lydda) and [Ramle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramle "Ramle"). In a second planned stage of the operation the fortified positions of [Latrun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latrun "Latrun") – overlooking the Tel Aviv-Jerusalem highway – and the city of [Ramallah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramallah "Ramallah") were also to be captured. [Hadita](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hadita&action=edit&redlink=1 "Hadita (page does not exist)"), near Latrun, was captured by the Israelis at a cost of nine dead.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/LyddaAirportCapture.png/220px-LyddaAirportCapture.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:LyddaAirportCapture.png)

Israeli armoured vehicles in [Lydda airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lod_airport "Lod airport") after the town's capture by Israeli forces

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ramla_prisoners_of_war%2C_July_12-13%2C_1948.png/220px-Ramla_prisoners_of_war%2C_July_12-13%2C_1948.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ramla_prisoners_of_war,_July_12-13,_1948.png)

Arab [prisoners of war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoners_of_war "Prisoners of war") captured by Israeli forces in [Ramla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramla "Ramla").

The objectives of Operation Danny were to capture territory east of Tel Aviv and then to push inland and relieve the Jewish population and forces in [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem"). Lydda had become an important military center in the region, lending support to Arab military activities elsewhere, and Ramle was one of the main obstacles blocking Jewish transportation. Lydda was defended by a local militia of around 1,000 residents, with an [Arab Legion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Legion "Arab Legion") contingent of 125–300.<sup id="cite_ref-207"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-207">[203]</a></sup>

The IDF forces gathered to attack the city numbered around 8,000. It was the first operation where several brigades were involved. The city was attacked from the north via [Majdal al-Sadiq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majdal_al-Sadiq "Majdal al-Sadiq") and [al-Muzayri'a](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Muzayri%27a "Al-Muzayri'a"), and from the east via [Khulda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khulda "Khulda"), [al-Qubab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qubab "Al-Qubab"), [Jimzu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimzu "Jimzu") and [Daniyal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniyal "Daniyal"). Bombers were also used for the first time in the conflict to bombard the city. The IDF captured the city on 11 July.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p64_193-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p64-193">[189]</a></sup>

Up to 450 Arabs and 9–10 Israeli soldiers were killed.
