The next day, Ramle fell.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p64_193-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p64-193">[189]</a></sup> The civilian populations of Lydda and Ramle [fled or were expelled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Palestinian_expulsion_from_Lydda_and_Ramle "1948 Palestinian expulsion from Lydda and Ramle") to the Arab front lines, and following resistance in Lydda, the population there was expelled without provision of transport vehicles; some of the evictees died on the long walk under the hot July sun.<sup id="cite_ref-208"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-208">[204]</a></sup>

On 15–16 July, an attack on Latrun took place but did not manage to occupy the fort.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p64_193-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p64-193">[189]</a></sup> A desperate second attempt occurred on 18 July by units from the [Yiftach Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yiftach_Brigade "Yiftach Brigade") equipped with armoured vehicles, including two [Cromwell tanks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cromwell_tank "Cromwell tank"), but that attack also failed. Despite the second truce, which began on 18 July, the Israeli efforts to conquer Latrun continued until 20 July.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

#### Jerusalem

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/PikiWiki_Israel_2184_1948_war_%D7%9E%D7%9C%D7%97%D7%9E%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%A2%D7%A6%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%95%D7%AA.jpg/220px-PikiWiki_Israel_2184_1948_war_%D7%9E%D7%9C%D7%97%D7%9E%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%A2%D7%A6%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%95%D7%AA.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_2184_1948_war_%D7%9E%D7%9C%D7%97%D7%9E%D7%AA_%D7%94%D7%A2%D7%A6%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%95%D7%AA.jpg)

[Beit Horon Battalion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Etzioni_Brigade "Etzioni Brigade") soldiers in the [Russian Compound](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Compound "Russian Compound") in Jerusalem, 1948

[Operation Kedem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Kedem "Operation Kedem")'s aim was to secure the Old City of Jerusalem, but fewer resources were allocated. The operation failed.<sup id="cite_ref-209"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-209">[205]</a></sup> Originally the operation was to begin on 8 July, immediately after the first truce, by [Irgun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irgun "Irgun") and [Lehi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lehi_(group) "Lehi (group)") forces. However, it was delayed by [David Shaltiel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Shaltiel "David Shaltiel"), possibly because he did not trust their ability after their failure to capture [Deir Yassin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deir_Yassin "Deir Yassin") without Haganah assistance.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

Irgun forces commanded by [Yehuda Lapidot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yehuda_Lapidot "Yehuda Lapidot") were to break through at the [New Gate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Gate "New Gate"), Lehi was to break through the wall stretching from the New Gate to the [Jaffa Gate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaffa_Gate "Jaffa Gate"), and the [Beit Horon Battalion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Etzioni_Brigade "Etzioni Brigade") was to strike from [Mount Zion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Zion "Mount Zion").<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

The battle was planned to begin on the [Shabbat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shabbat "Shabbat"), at 20:00 on 16 July, two days before the second ceasefire of the war. The plan went wrong from the beginning and was postponed first to 23:00 and then to midnight. It was not until 02:30 that the battle actually began. The Irgun managed to break through at the New Gate, but the other forces failed in their missions. At 05:45 on 17 July, Shaltiel ordered a retreat and to cease hostilities.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

On 14 July 1948, Irgun occupied the Arab village of [Malha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malha "Malha") after a fierce battle. Several hours later, the Arabs launched a counterattack, but Israeli reinforcements arrived, and the village was retaken at a cost of 17 dead.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

#### Southern Galilee

The second plan was [Operation Dekel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Dekel "Operation Dekel"), which was aimed at capturing the [Lower Galilee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Galilee "Lower Galilee") including [Nazareth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazareth "Nazareth"). Nazareth was captured on 16 July, and by the time the second truce took effect at 19:00 18 July, the whole Lower Galilee from Haifa Bay to the [Sea of Galilee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_of_Galilee "Sea of Galilee") was captured by Israel.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

#### Eastern Galilee

Operation Brosh was launched in a failed attempt to dislodge Syrian forces from the Eastern Galilee and the Benot Yaakov Bridge. During the operation, 200 Syrians and 100 Israelis were killed.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

### Second truce: 18 July – 15 October 1948

At 19:00 on 18 July, the second truce of the conflict went into effect after intense diplomatic efforts by the UN.

On 16 September, Count [Folke Bernadotte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folke_Bernadotte "Folke Bernadotte") proposed a new partition for Palestine in which the [Negev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev "Negev") would be divided between Jordan and Egypt, and Jordan would annexe [Lydda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lod "Lod") and [Ramla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramla "Ramla"). There would be a Jewish state in the whole of [Galilee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galilee "Galilee"), with the frontier running from Faluja northeast towards Ramla and Lydda. [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem") would be internationalised, with municipal autonomy for the city's Jewish and Arab inhabitants, the [Port of Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_of_Haifa "Port of Haifa") would be a free port, and [Lydda Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Gurion_International_Airport "Ben Gurion International Airport") would be a free airport. All [Palestinian refugees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_refugee "Palestinian refugee") would be granted the [right of return](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_of_return "Right of return"), and those who chose not to return would be compensated for lost property. The UN would control and regulate Jewish immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p76_210-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p76-210">[206]</a></sup>

The plan was once again rejected by both sides. On the next day, 17 September, Bernadotte was [assassinated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folke_Bernadotte#Assassination "Folke Bernadotte") in Jerusalem by the militant Zionist group [Lehi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lehi_(group) "Lehi (group)"). A four-man team ambushed Bernadotte's motorcade in Jerusalem, killing him and a French UN observer sitting next to him. Lehi saw Bernadotte as a British and Arab puppet, and thus a serious threat to the emerging State of Israel, and feared that the provisional Israeli government would accept the plan, which it considered disastrous. Unbeknownst to Lehi, the government had already decided to reject it and resume combat in a month. Bernadotte's deputy, American [Ralph Bunche](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ralph_Bunche "Ralph Bunche"), replaced him.<sup id="cite_ref-211"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-211">[207]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-212">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Haberman1995_213-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Haberman1995-213">[209]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cowell1991_214-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Cowell1991-214">[210]</a></sup>

On 22 September 1948, the [Provisional State Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provisional_State_Council "Provisional State Council") of Israel passed the Area of Jurisdiction and Powers Ordnance, 5708–1948. The law officially added to Israel's size by annexing all land it had captured since the war began. It also declared that from then on, any part of Palestine captured by the Israeli army would automatically become part of Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-215"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-215">[211]</a></sup>

### Little triangle pocket

The Arab villagers of the area known as the "[Little Triangle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triangle_(Israel) "Triangle (Israel)")" south of [Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa") repeatedly fired at Israeli traffic along the main road from [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv") to [Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa") and were supplied by the Iraqis from northern Samaria.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p298_216-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p298-216">[212]</a></sup> The sniping at traffic continued during the Second Truce. The poorly-planned assaults on 18 June and 8 July had failed to dislodge Arab militia from their superior positions. The Israelis launched [Operation Shoter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Shoter "Operation Shoter") on 24 July in order to gain control of the main road to Haifa and to destroy all the enemy in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p298_216-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p298-216">[212]</a></sup>

Israeli assaults on 24 and 25 July were beaten back with stiff resistance. The Israelis then broke the Arab defences with a combined infantry and armour assault backed by heavy shelling and bombing. Three Arab villages surrendered, and most of the inhabitants fled before and during the attack. The Israeli soldiers and aircraft struck one of the Arab retreat routes, killing 60 Arab soldiers.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="Summary of problem (December 2013)">dubious</span></a> <span>– <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#the_article_has_POV_and_%22dubious%22_problems" title="Talk:1948 Arab–Israeli War">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup>. Most of the inhabitants fled before and during the attack, reaching northern Samaria; hundreds were forcibly expelled during the following days. At least a hundred militiamen and civilians were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p298_216-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p298-216">[212]</a></sup>

The Arabs claimed that the Israelis had massacred Arab civilians, but the Israelis rejected the claims.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="Summary of problem (December 2013)">dubious</span></a> <span>– <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#the_article_has_POV_and_%22dubious%22_problems" title="Talk:1948 Arab–Israeli War">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> A United Nations investigation found no evidence of a massacre. Following the operation, the Tel Aviv-Haifa road was opened to Israeli military and civilian traffic, and Arab roadblocks along the route were removed. Traffic along the Haifa-[Hadera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hadera "Hadera") coastal railway was also restored.

### Third phase: 15 October 1948 – 10 March 1949

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/1948_arab_israeli_war_-_Oct.jpg/250px-1948_arab_israeli_war_-_Oct.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1948_arab_israeli_war_-_Oct.jpg)

October battles

Israel launched a series of military operations to drive out the Arab armies and secure the northern and southern borders of Israel.

#### Northern front – Galilee

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Zionist_mortar_team_outside_Zafzaf_in_October_1948.png/150px-Zionist_mortar_team_outside_Zafzaf_in_October_1948.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Zionist_mortar_team_outside_Zafzaf_in_October_1948.png)

An Israeli mortar team outside [Safsaf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safsaf "Safsaf"), October 1948

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Israeli_soldiers_in_battle_with_the_Arab_village_of_Sassa.jpg/220px-Israeli_soldiers_in_battle_with_the_Arab_village_of_Sassa.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Israeli_soldiers_in_battle_with_the_Arab_village_of_Sassa.jpg)

Israeli soldiers attack Sasa during Operation Hiram, October 1948.

On 22 October, the third truce went into effect.<sup id="cite_ref-217"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-217">[213]</a></sup> Irregular Arab forces refused to recognise the truce, and continued to harass Israeli forces and settlements in the north. On the same day that the truce came into effect, the [Arab Liberation Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Liberation_Army "Arab Liberation Army") violated the truce by attacking [Manara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manara,_Israel "Manara, Israel"), capturing the strongpoint of Sheikh Abed, repulsing counterattacks by local Israeli units, and ambushed Israeli forces attempting to relieve Manara. The IDF's [Carmeli Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carmeli_Brigade "Carmeli Brigade") lost 33 dead and 40 wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-218"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-218">[214]</a></sup> Manara and [Misgav Am](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Misgav_Am "Misgav Am") were totally cut off, and Israel's protests at the UN failed to change the situation.

On 24 October, the IDF launched [Operation Hiram](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Hiram "Operation Hiram") and captured the entire [upper Galilee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Galilee "Upper Galilee") area, driving the ALA back to Lebanon, and ambushing and destroying an entire Syrian battalion.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup> The Israeli force of four infantry brigades was commanded by [Moshe Carmel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moshe_Carmel "Moshe Carmel").<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup> The entire operation lasted just 60 hours, during which numerous villages were captured, often after locals or Arab forces put up resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup> Arab losses were estimated at 400 dead and 550 taken prisoner, with low Israeli casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup>

Some prisoners were reportedly executed by the Israeli forces. An estimated 50,000 Palestinian refugees fled into Lebanon, some of them fleeing ahead of the advancing forces, and some expelled from villages which had resisted, while the Arab inhabitants of those villages which had remained at peace were allowed to remain and became Israeli citizens. The villagers of [Iqrit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iqrit "Iqrit") and Birim were persuaded to leave their homes by Israeli authorities, who promised them that they would be allowed to return. Israel eventually decided not to allow them to return, and offered them financial compensation, which they refused to accept.<sup id="cite_ref-220"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-220">[216]</a></sup>

At the end of the month, the IDF had captured the whole of Galilee, driven all ALA forces out of Israel, and had advanced 8 kilometres (5 miles) into [Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanon "Lebanon") to the [Litani River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Litani_River "Litani River"),<sup id="cite_ref-Operation_Hiram_221-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Operation_Hiram-221">[217]</a></sup> occupying thirteen Lebanese villages. In the village of [Hula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hula,_Lebanon "Hula, Lebanon"), two Israeli officers [killed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hula_massacre "Hula massacre") between 35 and 58 prisoners as retaliation for the [Haifa Oil Refinery massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa_Oil_Refinery_massacre "Haifa Oil Refinery massacre"). Both officers were later put on trial for their actions.

#### Negev

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Israelis_at_Faluja.jpg/220px-Israelis_at_Faluja.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Israelis_at_Faluja.jpg)

Israeli troops occupying abandoned Egyptian trenches at [Huleiqat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huleiqat "Huleiqat"), October 1948

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Beersheba_1948.jpg/220px-Beersheba_1948.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Beersheba_1948.jpg)

IDF forces in [Beersheba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beersheba "Beersheba") during [Operation Yoav](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Yoav "Operation Yoav")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Negev_Brigade_soldiers_1948.jpg/220px-Negev_Brigade_soldiers_1948.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Negev_Brigade_soldiers_1948.jpg)

An IDF artillery unit in the Negev

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Beit_Natif_1948.jpg/220px-Beit_Natif_1948.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Beit_Natif_1948.jpg)

IDF forces near [Bayt Nattif](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayt_Nattif "Bayt Nattif"), near Hebron, after it was captured. October 1948.

Israel launched a series of military operations to drive out the Arab armies and secure the borders of Israel. However, invading the West Bank might have brought into the borders of the expanding State of Israel a massive Arab population it could not absorb. The Negev desert was an empty space for expansion, so the main war effort shifted to Negev from early October.<sup id="cite_ref-222"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-222">[218]</a></sup> Israel decided to destroy or at least drive out the Egyptian expeditionary force since the Egyptian front lines were too vulnerable as permanent borders.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris2008p320_223-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2008p320-223">[219]</a></sup>

On 15 October, the IDF launched [Operation Yoav](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Yoav "Operation Yoav") in the northern Negev.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p64_193-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p64-193">[189]</a></sup> Its goal was to drive a wedge between the Egyptian forces along the coast and the [Beersheba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beersheba "Beersheba")\-[Hebron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebron "Hebron")\-Jerusalem road and ultimately to conquer the whole Negev.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p64_193-8"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p64-193">[189]</a></sup> This was a special concern on the Israeli part because of a British diplomatic campaign to have the entire Negev handed over to Egypt and Jordan, and which thus made Ben-Gurion anxious to have Israeli forces in control of the Negev as soon as possible.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p64_193-9"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p64-193">[189]</a></sup>

Operation Yoav was headed by the Southern Front commander [Yigal Allon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yigal_Allon "Yigal Allon"). Committed to Yoav were three infantry and one armoured brigades, who were given the task of breaking through the Egyptian lines.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup> The Egyptian positions were badly weakened by the lack of a [defence in depth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defence_in_depth "Defence in depth"), which meant that once the IDF had broken through the Egyptian lines, there was little to stop them.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup> The operation was a huge success, shattering the Egyptian ranks and forcing the Egyptian Army from the northern Negev, [Beersheba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beersheba "Beersheba") and [Ashdod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashdod "Ashdod").<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup>

In the so-called "[Faluja Pocket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faluja_Pocket "Faluja Pocket")", an encircled Egyptian force was able to hold out for four months until the [1949 Armistice Agreements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements "1949 Armistice Agreements"), when the village was peacefully transferred to Israel and the Egyptian troops left.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup> Four warships of the [Israeli Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Navy "Israeli Navy") provided support by bombarding Egyptian shore installations in the [Ashkelon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashkelon "Ashkelon") area, and preventing the [Egyptian Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_Navy "Egyptian Navy") from evacuating retreating Egyptian troops by sea.<sup id="cite_ref-navy_190-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-navy-190">[186]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (June 2022)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

On 19 October, [Operation Ha-Har](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Ha-Har "Operation Ha-Har") began in the [Jerusalem Corridor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem_Corridor "Jerusalem Corridor"), while a [naval battle also took place](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_naval_campaign_in_Operation_Yoav#Battle_near_Majdal "Israeli naval campaign in Operation Yoav") near [Majdal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Majdal,_Askalan "Al-Majdal, Askalan"), with three Israeli corvettes facing an Egyptian corvette with air support. An Israeli sailor was killed and four wounded, and two of the ships were damaged. One Egyptian plane was shot down, but the corvette escaped. Israeli naval vessels also shelled Majdal on 17 October, and [Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_City "Gaza City") on 21 October, with air support from the [Israeli Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force "Israeli Air Force"). The same day, the IDF [captured Beersheba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Beersheba_(1948) "Battle of Beersheba (1948)"), and took 120 Egyptian soldiers prisoner. On 22 October, Israeli naval commandos using explosive boats [sank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_naval_campaign_in_Operation_Yoav "Israeli naval campaign in Operation Yoav") the Egyptian flagship _[Emir Farouk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Amir_Farouq "El Amir Farouq")_, and damaged an Egyptian minesweeper.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-8"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup>

On 9 November 1948, the IDF launched [Operation Shmone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Shmone "Operation Shmone") to capture the [Tegart fort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tegart_fort "Tegart fort") in the village of [Iraq Suwaydan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq_Suwaydan "Iraq Suwaydan"). The fort's Egyptian defenders had previously repulsed eight attempts to take it, including two during Operation Yoav. Israeli forces bombarded the fort before an assault with artillery and airstrikes by B-17 bombers. After breaching the outlying fences without resistance, the Israelis blew a hole in the fort's outer wall, prompting the 180 Egyptian soldiers manning the fort to surrender without a fight. The defeat prompted the Egyptians to evacuate several nearby positions, including hills the IDF had failed to take by force. Meanwhile, IDF forces took Iraq Suwaydan itself after a fierce battle, losing 6 dead and 14 wounded.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

From 5 to 7 December, the IDF conducted [Operation Assaf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Assaf "Operation Assaf") to take control of the Western Negev. The main assaults were spearheaded by mechanised forces, while [Golani Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golani_Brigade "Golani Brigade") infantry covered the rear. An Egyptian counterattack was repulsed. The Egyptians planned another counterattack, but it failed after Israeli aerial reconnaissance revealed Egyptian preparations, and the Israelis launched a preemptive strike. About 100 Egyptians were killed, and 5 tanks were destroyed, with the Israelis losing 5 killed and 30 wounded.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Operation_Horev.jpg/220px-Operation_Horev.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Operation_Horev.jpg)

An Israeli convoy in the Negev during Operation Horev

On 22 December, the IDF launched [Operation Horev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Horev "Operation Horev"), also called Operation Ayin.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-9"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup> The goal of the operation was to drive all remaining Egyptian forces from the Negev, destroying the Egyptian threat on Israel's southern communities and forcing the Egyptians into a ceasefire. During five days of fighting, the Israelis secured the Western Negev, expelling all Egyptian forces from the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-10"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup>

Israeli forces subsequently launched raids into the [Nitzana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitzana,_Israel "Nitzana, Israel") area, and entered the [Sinai Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_the_Sinai_(1948) "Battles of the Sinai (1948)") on 28 December. The IDF captured Umm Katef and [Abu Ageila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Ageila "Abu Ageila"), and advanced north towards [Al Arish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arish "Arish"), with the goal of encircling the entire Egyptian expeditionary force. Israeli forces pulled out of the Sinai on 2 January 1949 following joint British-American pressure and a British threat of military action. IDF forces regrouped at the border with the [Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip"). Israeli forces attacked [Rafah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Rafah_(1948) "Battle of Rafah (1948)") the following day, and after several days of fighting, Egyptian forces in the Gaza Strip were surrounded. The Egyptians agreed to negotiate a ceasefire on 7 January, and the IDF subsequently pulled out of Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh2002p68_219-11"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Karsh2002p68-219">[215]</a></sup> According to Morris, "_the inequitable and unfair rules of engagement: the Arabs could launch offensives with impunity, but international interventions always hampered and restrained Israel's counterattacks."_<sup id="cite_ref-224"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-224">[220]</a></sup>

On 28 December, the [Alexandroni Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexandroni_Brigade "Alexandroni Brigade") failed to take the Falluja Pocket, but managed to seize Iraq el-Manshiyeh and temporarily hold it.<sup id="cite_ref-225"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-225">[221]</a></sup> The Egyptians counterattacked, but were mistaken for a friendly force and allowed to advance, trapping a large number of men. The Israelis lost 87 soldiers.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

On 5 March, [Operation Uvda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Uvda "Operation Uvda") was launched following nearly a month of reconnaissance, with the goal of securing the Southern Negev from Jordan. The IDF entered and secured the territory, but did not meet significant resistance along the way, as the area was already designated to be part of the Jewish state in the UN Partition Plan, and the operation meant to establish Israeli sovereignty over the territory rather than actually conquer it. The Golani, [Negev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev_Brigade "Negev Brigade"), and Alexandroni brigades participated in the operation, together with some smaller units and with naval support.<sup id="cite_ref-226"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-226">[222]</a></sup>

On 10 March, Israeli forces secured the Southern Negev, reaching the southern tip of Palestine: Umm Rashrash on the [Red Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Sea "Red Sea") (where [Eilat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eilat "Eilat") was built later) and taking it without a battle. Israeli soldiers raised a hand-made Israeli flag ("[The Ink Flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ink_Flag "Ink Flag")") at 16:00 on 10 March, claiming Umm Rashrash for Israel. The raising of the Ink Flag is considered to be the end of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-227"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-227">[223]</a></sup>

#### Anglo-Israeli air clashes

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ramle_Funeral_1949.jpg/220px-Ramle_Funeral_1949.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ramle_Funeral_1949.jpg)

The funeral of a [Royal Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Air_Force "Royal Air Force") pilot killed during a clash with the [Israeli Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force "Israeli Air Force")

As the fighting progressed and Israel mounted an incursion into the Sinai, the [Royal Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Air_Force "Royal Air Force") began conducting almost daily reconnaissance missions over Israel and the Sinai. RAF reconnaissance aircraft took off from Egyptian airbases and sometimes flew alongside [Royal Egyptian Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_Air_Force "Egyptian Air Force") planes. High-flying British aircraft frequently flew over [Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa") and [Ramat David Airbase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramat_David_Airbase "Ramat David Airbase"), and became known to the Israelis as the "shuftykeit."<sup id="cite_ref-spyflight_228-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-spyflight-228">[224]</a></sup>

On 20 November 1948, an unarmed RAF photo-reconnaissance [De Havilland Mosquito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_Havilland_Mosquito "De Havilland Mosquito") of [No. 13 Squadron RAF](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No._13_Squadron_RAF "No. 13 Squadron RAF") was shot down by an [Israeli Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force "Israeli Air Force") [P-51 Mustang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P-51_Mustang "P-51 Mustang") flown by American volunteer Wayne Peake as it flew over the [Galilee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galilee "Galilee") towards [Hatzor Airbase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hatzor_Airbase "Hatzor Airbase"). Peake opened fire with his cannons, causing a fire to break out in the port engine. The aircraft turned to sea and lowered its altitude, then exploded and crashed off [Ashdod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashdod "Ashdod"). The pilot and navigator were both killed.<sup id="cite_ref-spyflight_228-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-spyflight-228">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-229">[225]</a></sup>

Just before noon on 7 January 1949, four [Spitfire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire "Supermarine Spitfire") FR18s from [No. 208 Squadron RAF](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No._208_Squadron_RAF "No. 208 Squadron RAF") on a reconnaissance mission in the [Deir al-Balah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deir_al-Balah "Deir al-Balah") area flew over an Israeli convoy that had been attacked by five Egyptian Spitfires fifteen minutes earlier. The pilots had spotted smoking vehicles and were drawn to the scene out of curiosity. Two planes dived to below 500 feet altitude to take pictures of the convoy, while the remaining two covered them from 1,500 feet.<sup id="cite_ref-spyflight_228-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-spyflight-228">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aloni_230-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Aloni-230">[226]</a></sup>

Israeli soldiers on the ground, alerted by the sound of the approaching Spitfires and fearing another Egyptian air attack, opened fire with machine guns. One Spitfire was shot down by a tank-mounted machine gun, while the other was lightly damaged and rapidly pulled up. The remaining three Spitfires were then attacked by patrolling IAF Spitfires flown by [Chalmers Goodlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chalmers_Goodlin "Chalmers Goodlin") and John McElroy, volunteers from the United States and Canada respectively. All three Spitfires were shot down, and one pilot was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-spyflight_228-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-spyflight-228">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aloni_230-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Aloni-230">[226]</a></sup>

Two pilots were captured by Israeli soldiers and taken to [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv") for interrogation, and were later released. Another was rescued by [Bedouins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bedouin "Bedouin") and handed over to the Egyptian Army, which turned him over to the RAF. Later that day, four RAF Spitfires from the same squadron escorted by seven [Hawker Tempests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawker_Tempest "Hawker Tempest") from [No. 213 Squadron RAF](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No._213_Squadron_RAF "No. 213 Squadron RAF") and eight from [No. 6 Squadron RAF](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No._6_Squadron_RAF "No. 6 Squadron RAF") went searching for the lost planes, and were attacked by four IAF Spitfires. The Israeli formation was led by [Ezer Weizman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ezer_Weizman "Ezer Weizman"). The remaining three were manned by Weizman's wingman Alex Jacobs and American volunteers Bill Schroeder and Caesar Dangott.<sup id="cite_ref-spyflight_228-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-spyflight-228">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aloni_230-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Aloni-230">[226]</a></sup>

The Tempests found they could not jettison their external fuel tanks, and some had non-operational guns. Schroeder shot down a British Tempest, killing pilot David Tattersfield, and Weizman severely damaged a British plane flown by Douglas Liquorish. Weizman's plane and two other British aircraft suffered light damage during the engagement. During the battle, British Tempest pilots treated British Spitfires as potential Israeli aircraft until the British Spitfire pilots were told by radio to wiggle their wings to be more clearly identifiable. The engagement ended when the Israelis realised the danger of their situation and disengaged, returning to Hatzor Airbase.<sup id="cite_ref-spyflight_228-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-spyflight-228">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aloni_230-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Aloni-230">[226]</a></sup>

Israeli Prime Minister [David Ben-Gurion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion "David Ben-Gurion") personally ordered the wrecks of the RAF fighters that had been shot down to be dragged into Israeli territory. Israeli troops subsequently visited the crash sites, removed various parts, and buried the other aircraft. However, the Israelis did not manage to conceal the wrecks in time to prevent British reconnaissance planes from photographing them. An RAF salvage team was deployed to recover the wrecks, entering Israeli territory during their search. Two were discovered inside Egypt, while Tattersfield's Tempest was found north of [Nirim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nirim "Nirim"), 6 km (4 mi) inside Israel. Interviews with local Arabs confirmed that the Israelis had visited the crash sites to remove and bury the wrecks. Tattersfield was initially buried near the wreckage, but his body was later removed and reburied at the British War Cemetery in [Ramla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramla "Ramla").<sup id="cite_ref-spyflight_228-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-spyflight-228">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cohen_231-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-cohen-231">[227]</a></sup>

In response, the RAF readied all Tempests and Spitfires to attack any IAF aircraft they encountered and bomb IAF airfields. British troops in the Middle East were placed on high alert with all leave cancelled, and British citizens were advised to leave Israel. The [Royal Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Navy "Royal Navy") was placed on high alert. At Hatzor Airbase, the general consensus among the pilots, most of whom had flown with or alongside the RAF during World War II, was that the RAF would not allow the loss of five aircraft and two pilots to go without retaliation, and would probably attack the base at dawn the next day. That night, in anticipation of an impending British attack, some pilots decided not to offer any resistance and left the base, while others prepared their Spitfires and were strapped into the cockpits at dawn, preparing to repel a retaliatory airstrike. However, despite pressure from the squadrons involved in the incidents, British commanders refused to authorise any retaliatory strikes.<sup id="cite_ref-spyflight_228-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-spyflight-228">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-232">[228]</a></sup>

The day following the incident, British pilots were issued a directive to regard any Israeli aircraft infiltrating Egyptian or Jordanian airspace as hostile and to shoot them down, but were also ordered to avoid activity close to Israel's borders. Later in January 1949, the British managed to prevent the delivery of aviation spirit and other essential fuels to Israel in retaliation for the incident. The [British Foreign Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office "Foreign and Commonwealth Office") presented the Israeli government with a demand for compensation over the loss of personnel and equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-spyflight_228-8"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-spyflight-228">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-233">[229]</a></sup>

#### UN Resolution 194

In December 1948, the [UN General Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly "United Nations General Assembly") passed [Resolution 194](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_194 "United Nations General Assembly Resolution 194"). It called to establish a [UN Conciliation Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Conciliation_Commission "United Nations Conciliation Commission") to facilitate peace between Israel and Arab states. However, many of the resolution's articles were not fulfilled, since these were opposed by Israel, rejected by the Arab states, or were overshadowed by war as the 1948 conflict continued.

## Weapons

Largely leftover World War II era weapons were used by both sides. Egypt had some British equipment; the Syrian army had some French. German, Czechoslovak and British equipment was used by Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-234"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-234">[230]</a></sup>

According to Amitzur Ilan, "Israel's ability to cope better with the embargo situation was, by far, her greatest strategic asset."<sup id="cite_ref-235"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-235">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-236">[232]</a></sup>

| Type | Arab armies | IDF |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Tanks | [Matilda tanks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matilda_II_tank "Matilda II tank"), [R-39s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renault_R40 "Renault R40"), [FT-17s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FT-17 "FT-17"), [R35s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renault_R35 "Renault R35"), [Panzer IVs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panzer_IV "Panzer IV") (dug in and used as stationary gun emplacements by Egypt), [Fiat M13/40](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiat_M13/40 "Fiat M13/40"), [Sherman M4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sherman_tank "Sherman tank"), [M-22](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M22_Locust "M22 Locust"), [Vickers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vickers "Vickers") [MK-6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_Tank_Mk_VI "Light Tank Mk VI"). | [Cromwell tanks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cromwell_tank "Cromwell tank"), [H39s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hotchkiss_H35 "Hotchkiss H35"), [M4 Sherman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M4_Sherman "M4 Sherman") |
| [APCs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armored_personnel_carrier "Armored personnel carrier")/[IFVs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infantry_fighting_vehicle "Infantry fighting vehicle") | British World War II era trucks, [Humber Mk III & IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humber_Armoured_Car "Humber Armoured Car"), Automitrailleuses Dodge/Bich type, improvised armored cars/trucks, [Marmon-Herrington Armoured Cars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marmon-Herrington_Armoured_Car "Marmon-Herrington Armoured Car"), [Universal Carriers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Carrier "Universal Carrier"), [Lloyd Towing Carriers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carden_Loyd_tankette "Carden Loyd tankette") | British World War II era trucks, improvised armored cars/trucks, [White M3A1 Scout Cars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M3_Scout_Car "M3 Scout Car"), [Daimler Armoured Cars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daimler_Armoured_Car "Daimler Armoured Car"), [Universal Carriers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Carrier "Universal Carrier"), [M3 Half-tracks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M3_Half-track "M3 Half-track"), [IHC M14 Half-tracks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IHC_M14_Half-track "IHC M14 Half-track"), [M5 Half-tracks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M5_Half-track "M5 Half-track") |
| Artillery | [Mortars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mortar_(weapon) "Mortar (weapon)"), [15 cm sIG33 auf Pz IIs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/15_cm_sIG_33_auf_Fahrgestell_Panzerkampfwagen_II_(Sf) "15 cm sIG 33 auf Fahrgestell Panzerkampfwagen II (Sf)"), [25 mm anti-tank guns on Bren carriers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Carrier "Universal Carrier"), improvised self-propelled guns used by Syrians in 1948–49, 65 mm mountain guns on [Lorraine 38L](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorraine_37L "Lorraine 37L") _chenillettes_, 2-pounder anti-tank guns, 6-pounder anti-tank guns | Mortars, 2-inch (51 mm) British mortars, 65 mm French howitzers (_[Napoleonchiks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonchik "Napoleonchik")_), [120 mm French mortars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/120_mm_French_mortars "120 mm French mortars"), [Davidka mortars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Davidka "Davidka") |
| Aircraft | [Spitfires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire "Supermarine Spitfire"), [T-6 Texans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T-6_Texan "T-6 Texan"), [C-47 Dakotas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C-47_Dakota "C-47 Dakota"), [Hawker Hurricanes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawker_Hurricane "Hawker Hurricane"), [Avro Ansons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avro_Anson "Avro Anson") | [Spitfires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire "Supermarine Spitfire"), [Avia S-199s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avia_S-199 "Avia S-199"), [B-17 Flying Fortresses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B-17_Flying_Fortress "B-17 Flying Fortress"), [P-51 Mustangs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P-51_Mustang "P-51 Mustang"), [C-47 Dakotas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C-47_Dakota "C-47 Dakota") |
| Small Arms | [Lee–Enfield rifles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lee%E2%80%93Enfield_rifle "Lee–Enfield rifle"), [Bren Guns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bren_Gun "Bren Gun"), [Sten guns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sten "Sten"), [MAS 36s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MAS_36 "MAS 36") | [Sten guns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sten "Sten"), [Mills grenades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mills_bomb "Mills bomb"), [Karabiner 98k](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karabiner_98k "Karabiner 98k") (Czech copies), [Bren Guns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bren_Gun "Bren Gun"), [MP 40s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MP_40 "MP 40"), [MG-34 Machine guns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MG-34 "MG-34"), [Thompson submachine guns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thompson_submachine_gun "Thompson submachine gun"), [Lee–Enfield rifles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lee%E2%80%93Enfield_rifle "Lee–Enfield rifle"), [Molotov cocktails](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molotov_cocktail "Molotov cocktail"), [PIAT anti-tank infantry weapon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PIAT "PIAT") |

## Israeli usage of biological warfare

Research by Israeli historians [Benny Morris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benny_Morris "Benny Morris") and [Benjamin Kedar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Kedar "Benjamin Kedar") show that during the 1948 war, Israel conducted a biological warfare operation codenamed "Cast Thy Bread." According to Morris and Kedar, the Haganah initially used typhoid bacteria to contaminate water wells in newly cleared Arab villages to prevent the population including militiamen from returning. Later, the biological warfare campaign expanded to include Jewish settlements that were in imminent danger of being captured by Arab troops and inhabited Arab towns not slated for capture. There were also plans to expand the biological warfare campaign into other Arab states including Egypt, Lebanon and Syria, but they were not carried out.<sup id="cite_ref-237"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-237">[233]</a></sup>

## Aftermath

### 1949 Armistice Agreements

[![Map comparing the borders of the 1947 partition plan and the Armistice Demarcation Lines of 1949.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/1947-UN-Partition-Plan-1949-Armistice-Comparison.svg/170px-1947-UN-Partition-Plan-1949-Armistice-Comparison.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1947-UN-Partition-Plan-1949-Armistice-Comparison.svg)

---

**Boundaries defined in the [1947 UN Partition Plan for Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine "United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine"):**

  Area assigned for a Jewish state

    Area assigned for an Arab state

---

**Armistice Demarcation Lines of 1949 ([Green Line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Line_(Israel) "Green Line (Israel)")):**

      Israeli controlled territory from 1949

In 1949, Israel signed separate [armistices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice "Armistice") with Egypt on 24 February, Lebanon on 23 March, Transjordan on 3 April, and Syria on 20 July. The Armistice Demarcation Lines, as set by the agreements, saw the territory under Israeli control encompassing approximately three-quarters of the prior British administered [Mandate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine "Mandatory Palestine") as it stood after [Transjordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan "Emirate of Transjordan")'s independence in 1946. Israel controlled territories of about one-third more than was allocated to the Jewish State under the UN partition proposal.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown2004_238-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Brown2004-238">[234]</a></sup> After the armistices, Israel had control over 78% of the territory comprising former Mandatory Palestine<sup id="cite_ref-239"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-239">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-240">[236]</a></sup> or some 21,000 km<sup>2</sup> (8,000 sq mi), including the entire [Galilee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galilee "Galilee") and [Jezreel Valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jezreel_Valley "Jezreel Valley") in the north, the whole [Negev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev "Negev") in south, [West Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Jerusalem "West Jerusalem") and the [coastal plain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_coastal_plain "Israeli coastal plain") in the center.

The armistice lines were known afterwards as the "[Green Line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Line_(Israel) "Green Line (Israel)")". The [Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip") and the [West Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank "West Bank") (including [East Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Jerusalem "East Jerusalem")) were occupied by Egypt and Transjordan respectively. The [United Nations Truce Supervision Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Truce_Supervision_Organization "United Nations Truce Supervision Organization") and [Mixed Armistice Commissions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixed_Armistice_Commissions "Mixed Armistice Commissions") were set up to monitor ceasefires, supervise the armistice agreements, to prevent isolated incidents from escalating, and assist other UN peacekeeping operations in the region.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

Just before the signing of the Israel-Transjordan armistice agreement, general Yigal Allon proposed a military offensive to conquer the West Bank up to the Jordan River as the natural, defensible border of the state. Ben-Gurion refused, although he was aware that the IDF was militarily strong enough to carry out the conquest. He feared the reaction of Western powers and wanted to maintain good relations with the United States and not to provoke the British. Moreover, the results of the war were already satisfactory and Israeli leaders had to build a state.<sup id="cite_ref-Shapira2014p173_241-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Shapira2014p173-241">[237]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Morris2009p79_242-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Morris2009p79-242">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shalom2002p174_243-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Shalom2002p174-243">[239]</a></sup>

### Casualties

Israel lost 6,373 of its people, about 1% of its population at the time, in the war. About 4,000 were soldiers and the rest were civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-politics_17-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-politics-17">[13]</a></sup>

The exact number of Arab casualties is unknown. One estimate places the Arab death toll at 7,000, including 3,000 Palestinians, 2,000 Egyptians, 1,000 Jordanians, and 1,000 Syrians.<sup id="cite_ref-onwar_120-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-onwar-120">[116]</a></sup> In 1958, Palestinian historian [Aref al-Aref](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aref_al-Aref "Aref al-Aref") calculated that the Arab armies' combined losses amounted to 3,700, with Egypt losing 961 regular and 200 irregular soldiers and Transjordan losing 362 regulars and 200 irregulars. According to [Henry Laurens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Laurens_(scholar) "Henry Laurens (scholar)"), the Palestinians suffered double the Jewish losses, with 13,000 dead, 1,953 of whom are known to have died in combat situations. Of the remainder, 4,004 remain nameless but the place, tally and date of their death is known, and a further 7,043, for whom only the place of death is known, not their identities nor the date of their death. According to Laurens, the largest part of Palestinian casualties consisted of non-combatants and corresponds to the successful operations of the Israelis.<sup id="cite_ref-laurens_18-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-laurens-18">[14]</a></sup>

### Demographic outcomes

#### Arabs

During the [1947–1948 Civil War in Mandatory Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947%E2%80%931948_Civil_War_in_Mandatory_Palestine "1947–1948 Civil War in Mandatory Palestine") and the 1948 Arab–Israeli War that followed, around 750,000 Palestinian Arabs fled or were expelled from their homes, out of approximately 1,200,000 Arabs living in former [British Mandate of Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine "Mandatory Palestine"), a displacement known to Palestinians as the _[Nakba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakba "Nakba")_. In 1951, the UN Conciliation Commission for Palestine estimated that the number of Palestinian refugees displaced from Israel was 711,000.<sup id="cite_ref-244"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-244">[240]</a></sup>

This number did not include [displaced Palestinians inside Israeli-held territory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Present_absentee "Present absentee"). More than 400 Arab villages, and about ten Jewish villages and neighbourhoods, [were depopulated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_villages_depopulated_during_the_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict "List of villages depopulated during the Arab–Israeli conflict") during the Arab–Israeli conflict, most of them during 1948. According to estimate based on earlier census, the total Muslim population in Palestine was 1,143,336 in 1947.<sup id="cite_ref-245"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-245">[241]</a></sup> The [causes of the 1948 Palestinian exodus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Causes_of_the_1948_Palestinian_exodus "Causes of the 1948 Palestinian exodus") are a controversial topic among historians.<sup id="cite_ref-246"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-246">[242]</a></sup> After the war, around 156,000 [Arabs remained](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_citizens_of_Israel "Arab citizens of Israel") in Israel and became Israeli citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-247"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-247">[243]</a></sup>

Displaced Palestinian Arabs, known as [Palestinian refugees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_refugee "Palestinian refugee"), were settled in [Palestinian refugee camps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestine_refugee_camps "Palestine refugee camps") throughout the Arab world. The United Nations established [UNRWA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNRWA "UNRWA") as a relief and human development agency tasked with providing humanitarian assistance to Palestinian refugees. Arab nations refused to absorb Palestinian refugees, instead keeping them in refugee camps while insisting that they be allowed to return.<sup id="cite_ref-Palestine_refugees-UNRWA_248-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Palestine_refugees-UNRWA-248">[244]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jerusalem_Fund_249-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Jerusalem_Fund-249">[245]</a></sup>

Refugee status was also passed on to their descendants, who were also largely denied citizenship in Arab states, except in Transjordan.<sup id="cite_ref-250"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-250">[246]</a></sup> The [Arab League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League") instructed its members to deny Palestinians citizenship "to avoid dissolution of their identity and protect their right of return to their homeland." More than 1.4 million Palestinians still live in 58 recognised refugee camps,<sup id="cite_ref-Palestine_refugees-UNRWA_248-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Palestine_refugees-UNRWA-248">[244]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jerusalem_Fund_249-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-Jerusalem_Fund-249">[245]</a></sup> while more than 5 million [Palestinians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinians#Demographics "Palestinians") live outside Israel and the [Palestinian territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_territories "Palestinian territories").

Palestinian refugees and displaced persons and the lack of a [Palestinian right of return](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_right_of_return "Palestinian right of return") remain major issues in the [Arab–Israeli conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict "Arab–Israeli conflict").

#### Jews

In the three years from May 1948 to the end of 1951, 700,000 Jews [settled in Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah "Aliyah"), mainly along the borders and in former Arab lands,<sup id="cite_ref-BennyMorris_32-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-BennyMorris-32">[28]</a></sup> doubling the Jewish population there.<sup id="cite_ref-251"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-251">[247]</a></sup> Of these, upwards of 300,000 [arrived from Asian and North African states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_Arab_and_Muslim_countries "Jewish exodus from Arab and Muslim countries").<sup id="cite_ref-sachar_pp395-403_252-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-sachar_pp395-403-252">[248]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-253">[249]</a></sup> Among them, the largest group, over 100,000, [was from Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Ezra_and_Nehemiah "Operation Ezra and Nehemiah"). The remaining came mostly from Europe, including 136,000 from the 250,000 displaced Jews of World War II living in [refugee camps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Displaced_persons_camps_in_post-World_War_II_Europe "Displaced persons camps in post-World War II Europe") and urban centers in Germany, Austria, and Italy,<sup id="cite_ref-254"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-254">[250]</a></sup> and more than 270,000 coming from Eastern Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-255"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-255">[251]</a></sup> mainly [Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Romania#Post-War "History of the Jews in Romania") and [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland#Communist_rule:_1945%E2%80%931989 "History of the Jews in Poland"), over 100,000 each.

On the establishment of the state, a top priority was given to a policy for the "ingathering of exiles", and the [Mossad LeAliyah Bet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mossad_LeAliyah_Bet "Mossad LeAliyah Bet") gave key assistance to the Jewish Agency to organise immigrants from Europe and the Middle East, and arrange for their transport to Israel. For Ben-Gurion, a fundamental defect of the State was that 'it lacked Jews'.<sup id="cite_ref-256"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-256">[252]</a></sup>

Jewish immigrants from Arab and Muslim countries left for numerous reasons. The war's outcome had exacerbated Arab hostilities to local Jewish communities. News of the victory aroused messianic expectations in Libya and Yemen; Zionism had taken root in many countries; active incentives for making aliyah formed a key part of Israeli policy; and better economic prospects and security were to be expected from a Jewish state.<sup id="cite_ref-sachar_pp395-403_252-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-sachar_pp395-403-252">[248]</a></sup>

Some Arab governments, Egypt, for example, held their Jewish communities hostage at times. Persecution, political instability, and news of a number of violent pogroms also played a role. Some 800,000–1,000,000 Jews eventually left the [Arab world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_world "Arab world") over the next three decades as a result of these various factors.<sup id="cite_ref-sachar_pp395-403_252-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-sachar_pp395-403-252">[248]</a></sup> An estimated 650,000 of the departees settled in [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeker20054_257-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeker20054-257">[253]</a></sup>

## Historiography

Since the war, different [historiographical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historiography "Historiography") traditions have interpreted the events of 1948 differently; in the words of the [New Historian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Historians "New Historians") [Avi Shlaim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avi_Shlaim "Avi Shlaim"), "each side subscribes to a different version of events."<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup> In the Israeli narrative, the war is Israel's War of Independence.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup> In the Palestinian narrative, the War of 1948 is inextricable from the [Nakba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakba "Nakba"), the Zionist movement is one of [settler colonialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionism_as_settler_colonialism "Zionism as settler colonialism"),<sup id="cite_ref-259"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-259">[255]</a></sup> and the Israelis are seen as [conquerors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conquest "Conquest") and the Palestinians as victims.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup> The different narratives of 1948 reflect these different perceptions.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup>

An issue affecting the historiography of 1948 is access to sources and archives, which may have been destroyed, appropriated, censored, or otherwise made unavailable to some or all researchers.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_260-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:2-260">[256]</a></sup> Linguistic barriers represent another hurdle, as most research is published exclusively in the author's native language and is not translated.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_260-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:2-260">[256]</a></sup>

The historiography of 1948 is tied to political [legitimacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legitimacy_(political) "Legitimacy (political)") in the present and has implications for the [Israeli–Palestinian conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict "Israeli–Palestinian conflict").<sup id="cite_ref-:1_261-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:1-261">[257]</a></sup> According to [Avraham Sela](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avraham_Sela "Avraham Sela") and Neil Caplan:

> A major reason for this grip of the past over the present is the unfulfilled quest of both Israelis and Palestinians for legitimacy, in one or more of the following three senses: (a) each party's sense of its own legitimacy as a national community entitled to its own sovereign state; (b) each party's willingness to grant legitimacy to at least part of the competing national narrative of the other; and (c) the international community's extension of legitimacy to the competing rights and claims of Israelis and Palestinians.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_261-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:1-261">[257]</a></sup>

The narratives of 1948 have also had implications for [Palestinian refugees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_refugees "Palestinian refugees").<sup id="cite_ref-:2_260-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:2-260">[256]</a></sup><sup><span title="Page: 211">: 211 </span></sup> 

### Israeli narratives

The Israelis, whether or not they were conquerors, were irrefutably the victors of the war, and for this reason among others, "they were able to propagate more effectively than their opponents their version of this fateful war."<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup> Only in 1987 was that narrative effectively challenged outside the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup>

#### Zionist narrative

Avi Shlaim gives the conventional Zionist narrative or the "old history" of the 1948 war as follows:

> The conflict between Jews and Arabs in Palestine came to a head following the passage, on 29 November 1947, of the United Nations partition resolution that called for the establishment of two states, one Jewish and one Arab. The Jews accepted the U.N. plan despite the painful sacrifices it entailed, but the Palestinians, the neighboring Arab states, and the Arab League rejected it. Great Britain did everything in its power toward the end of the Palestine Mandate to frustrate the establishment of the Jewish state envisaged in the UN plan. With the expiry of the Mandate and the proclamation of the State of Israel, seven Arab states sent their armies into Palestine with the firm intention of strangling the Jewish state at birth. The subsequent struggle was an unequal one between a Jewish David and an Arab Goliath. The infant Jewish state fought a desperate, heroic, and ultimately successful battle for survival against overwhelming odds. During the war, hundreds of thousands of Palestinians fled to the neighboring Arab states, mainly in response to orders from their leaders and despite Jewish pleas to stay and demonstrate that peaceful coexistence was possible. After the war, the story continues, Israeli leaders sought peace with all their heart and all their might but there was no one to talk to on the other side. Arab intransigence was alone responsible for the political deadlock, which was not broken until President Anwar Sadat's visit to Jerusalem thirty years later.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup>

According to Shlaim, this narrative is "not history in the proper sense of the word," as most of the literature on the war was produced – not by professional academic historians – but rather by participants in the war, politicians, soldiers, and state-sponsored historians, as well as by sympathetic journalists, chroniclers, and biographers.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-8"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup> It also portrays Israelis as morally superior, lacks political analysis, and gives undue weight to "the heroic feats of the Israeli fighters."<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-9"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup> This [nationalist narrative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist_historiography "Nationalist historiography") was taught in Israeli schools and used for gaining legitimacy internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-10"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup>

#### New Historians

The standard Zionist narrative of the war remained unchallenged outside the Arab world until the war's fortieth anniversary, when a number of critical books came out, including [Simha Flapan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simha_Flapan "Simha Flapan")'s _The Birth of Israel: Myths and Realities_ (1987), [Benny Morris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benny_Morris "Benny Morris")'s _The Birth of the Palestinian Refugee Problem_ (1987), [Ilan Pappé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilan_Papp%C3%A9 "Ilan Pappé")'s _Britain and the Arab-Israeli Conflict, 1948–51_ (1988), and Shlaim's _Collusion Across the Jordan: King Abdullah, the Zionist Movement and the Partition of Palestine_ (1988).<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-11"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup> These writers came to be known as [New Historians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Historians "New Historians") or "post-Zionists."_<sup id="cite_ref-:3_262-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:3-262">[258]</a></sup>_

According to Shlaim, the new historians disagreed with the Zionist narrative on six main points: British policy with regard to the Yishuv at the end of the Palestine Mandate, the military balance in 1948, the origins of the Palestinian refugee problem, the nature of relations between Israelis and Jordanians during the war, Arab aims in the war, and the reasons peace remained elusive after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-12"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup>

Among their most vitriolic critics was [Shabtai Teveth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shabtai_Teveth "Shabtai Teveth"), biographer of [David Ben-Gurion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion "David Ben-Gurion"), who published "The New Historians," a series of four weekly full-page articles attacking the new historians, in [Haaretz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haaretz "Haaretz") May 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-13"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup> Teveth claimed that the new historiography was flawed in its practice and that it was politically motived, that it was pro-Palestinian and aimed to [delegitimize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delegitimisation_of_Israel "Delegitimisation of Israel") the State of Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_258-14"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:02-258">[254]</a></sup>

#### Neo-Zionist narratives

[Ilan Pappé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilan_Papp%C3%A9 "Ilan Pappé") identifies a turn in predominant Israeli narratives about 1948 in September 2000. In the climate of the [Second Intifada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Intifada "Second Intifada") and in the [Post-9/11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-9/11 "Post-9/11") period, "not only were Israel's brutal military operations against the Palestinians during the new intifada seen as justified, but so was their systematic expulsion in 1948."<sup id="cite_ref-:3_262-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:3-262">[258]</a></sup> Evidence of the expulsions, massacres, and war crimes of 1948 brought to light by the New Historians could no longer be ignored, but writers of what Pappé calls a "neo-Zionist" narrative justified these as necessary or unavoidable.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_262-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:3-262">[258]</a></sup>

In this period, the focus of Israeli historical writing on 1948 shifted largely from its human impact back to its military aspects.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_262-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:3-262">[258]</a></sup> Neo-Zionist writers were given selective access to top-secret material, to which writers critical of Zionism would not have been given access, and much of their work was published by the [Israeli Ministry of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Ministry_of_Defense "Israeli Ministry of Defense").<sup id="cite_ref-:3_262-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:3-262">[258]</a></sup>

Among those Pappé associated with the neo-Zionist perspective were [Benny Morris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benny_Morris "Benny Morris") (who had become more outspokenly defensive of Zionism by this time), [Daniel Gutwein](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Daniel_Gutwein&action=edit&redlink=1 "Daniel Gutwein (page does not exist)") \[[he](https://he.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D7%93%D7%A0%D7%99%D7%90%D7%9C_%D7%92%D7%95%D7%98%D7%95%D7%95%D7%99%D7%99%D7%9F "he:דניאל גוטוויין")\], [Mordechai Bar-On](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mordechai_Bar-On "Mordechai Bar-On"), [Yoav Gelber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoav_Gelber "Yoav Gelber"), Tamir Goren, [Arnon Golan](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Arnon_Golan&action=edit&redlink=1 "Arnon Golan (page does not exist)") \[[he](https://he.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D7%90%D7%A8%D7%A0%D7%95%D7%9F_%D7%92%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%9F "he:ארנון גולן")\], Alon Kadish, and [Yoav Peleg](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Yoav_Peleg&action=edit&redlink=1 "Yoav Peleg (page does not exist)") \[[he](https://he.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D7%99%D7%95%D7%90%D7%91_%D7%A4%D7%9C%D7%92 "he:יואב פלג")\], as well as the journal [_Techelet_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azure_(magazine) "Azure (magazine)") .<sup id="cite_ref-:3_262-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:3-262">[258]</a></sup>

### Palestinian narratives

Unlike Israeli narratives that shifted over the decades, Palestinian narratives of 1948 have been more or less constant, focusing on Palestinians' indigenous rights to Palestine, Palestinian victimhood, dispossession, displacement, exile, statelessness, and more "unrequited grievances against colonialism and Zionism."<sup id="cite_ref-:2_260-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:2-260">[256]</a></sup><sup><span title="Pages: 209–211">: 209–211 </span></sup>  The term '[Nakba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakba "Nakba")' to describe the Palestinian catastrophe in the war of 1948 was coined in [Constantin Zureiq's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantin_Zureiq "Constantin Zureiq") 1948 book _[Ma'na an-Nakba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma%27na_an-Nakba "Ma'na an-Nakba")_.<sup id="cite_ref-263"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-263">[259]</a></sup> [Yoav Gelber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoav_Gelber "Yoav Gelber") identifies [Arif al-Arif's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aref_al-Aref "Aref al-Aref") six volume _[an-Nakba](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=An-Nakba_(book)&action=edit&redlink=1 "An-Nakba (book) (page does not exist)")_  \[[ar](https://ar.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%86%D9%83%D8%A8%D8%A9_(%D9%83%D8%AA%D8%A7%D8%A8) "ar:النكبة (كتاب)")\] written in Arabic in the 1950s as thorough and notable.<sup id="cite_ref-264"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-264">[260]</a></sup>

Palestinian narratives have focused on countering the dominant Zionist narrative; the preeminent Palestinian historian of 1948 [Walid Khalidi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walid_Khalidi "Walid Khalidi") has dedicated much of his career to disproving the official Israeli narrative that the [1948 Palestinian expulsion and flight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Palestinian_expulsion_and_flight "1948 Palestinian expulsion and flight") was voluntary.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_260-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#cite_note-:2-260">[256]</a></sup><sup><span title="Page: 211">: 211 </span></sup>
